### Vertical Group  

Vertical Group = Who the customer is  
This is the customer category.  
Startup	Likely Channel  
Early startup	**EMG** / **SME** **DIGITAL**  
Scaling startup	**SME** **BROKING**  
Big startup	**CSG** / **CORP**  
recommendation for your project  
Use this as your standard:  
If age <= 10 years **AND** turnover < **200** crore **AND** startup-like/innovation-led:  
    Emerging  

    If revenue <= 1 crore **AND** assets <= 2 crore:  
    Emerging-0 (Pre-revenue / very early)  
    Else if revenue <= 10 crore **AND** assets <= 5 crore:  
    Emerging-1 (Early revenue)  
    Else if revenue <= 50 crore **AND** assets <= 25 crore:  
    Emerging-2 (Growth startup)  
    Else:  
    Emerging-3 (Scale-up startup)  

Else if turnover <= **500** crore **AND** assets <= **125** crore:  
    **SME**  

Else:  
    Corporate

Below is a deep, quantified, decision-oriented portfolio analysis of Business Shield â€“ **1010**.  
________________________________________  
## Executive Summary  
- Top-line decline with sharp quality deterioration:  
**GWP** declined 1,**359** â†’ 1,**270** (-89, -6.6%), but UW result flipped from +69 to -35 (-**104**) â†’ clear profitability collapse.  
- **NEP** contraction is severe:  
**NEP** reduced **376** â†’ **267** (-**109**, -29%), much sharper than **GWP** decline â†’ reinsurance + reserve dynamics heavily impacted earning base.  
- Claims improved in absolute terms but ratios worsened:  
**NIC** After **IBNR** fell **314** â†’ **194** (-**120**, -38%), yet Incurred LR deteriorated 65% â†’ 69% (+4 pts) due to lower **NEP**.  
- Massive reduction in **IBNR** (71 â†’ 9, -87%)  
â†’ Indicates reserve release dependence in PY but not sustainable in CY.  
- Expense ratio spike is the biggest driver of deterioration:  
Expense ratio jumped 40% â†’ 50% (+10 pts); total expenses rose **112** â†’ **130** (+16%) despite lower business â†’ operating inefficiency.  
- **COR** moved from profitable 81% to loss-making **115**% (+34 pts)  
â†’ Portfolio is structurally loss-making now.  
- Mumbai is the single largest negative driver:  
UW result collapsed +**119** â†’ -94 (-**213**) â†’ catastrophic deterioration.  
- Bangalore turnaround is the biggest positive shift:  
UW result improved -52 â†’ +26 (+78) due to claims collapse (LR **213**% â†’ 13%).  
- Retail vertical drove turnaround, Corporate remained stable, **SME** deteriorated:  
Retail UW result: -45 â†’ +19 (+64).  
- Growth quality is poor in key markets (Delhi, Mumbai, Kolkata) due to expense leakage and loss deterioration.  
- Significant reliance on volatile claims / **IBNR** movements across locations.  
- Emerging/**SME** (startup-like segments) showing weak economics (**COR** **116**%) â†’ not yet scalable profitably.  
________________________________________  
## Overall Portfolio Analysis â€“ Business Shield 1010  
Premium & Reinsurance  
- **GWP**: 1,**359** â†’ 1,**270** (-6.6%)  
- Prop ceding: 1,**011** â†’ **944** (-6.6%) â†’ stable ceding ratio (~74%)  
- **NWP**: **277** â†’ **259** (-6.5%) â†’ proportional decline  
âś… No major structural change in ceding, but:  
- RI Commission dropped: **332** â†’ **253** (-79, -24%)  
â†’ Major loss of income support.  
________________________________________  
Earnings (**NEP**) Dynamics  
- **NEP**: **376** â†’ **267** (-**109**, -29%)  
Drivers:  
- PY **URR** fell **213** â†’ **114** (-99)  
- **URR** charge almost flat **343** â†’ **331**  
âžˇď¸Ź Lower carry-forward earnings and reduced releases = thinner earned premium base  
________________________________________  
Claims & Reserves  
- **NIC** Before **IBNR**: **243** â†’ **185** (-24%)  
- **IBNR**: 71 â†’ 9 (-87%)  
- **NIC** After **IBNR**: **314** â†’ **194** (-38%)  
âś… Absolute claims improved, **BUT**:  
- Financial LR: 83% â†’ 73% (improvement)  
- Incurred LR: 65% â†’ 69% (deterioration)  
âš ď¸Ź Contradiction:  
Improved claim cost, but worse LR â†’ due to **NEP** compression  
âžˇď¸Ź **IBNR** collapse indicates PY reserve support, not sustainable improvement  
________________________________________

## Underwriting Perspective  
### Overall View  
- Portfolio quality worsened materially  
- Profitability in PY supported by:  
o	High RI commission  
o	High **IBNR** reserves  
- CY shows:  
o	Lower RI support  
o	Lower reserves  
â†’ true underlying loss emerging

### Location Classification  
âś… Scale Aggressively

âś… Grow Selectively

âš ď¸Ź Hold / Monitor

đźš¨ De-risk / Tighten

### Key Underwriting Insights  
- Claims volatility extremely high across locations (Mumbai, Bangalore, Location 9)  
â†’ indicates poor risk selection OR lumpy large losses  
- Expense inflation is systemic  
â†’ biggest driver of deterioration (not claims alone)  
- **IBNR** dependency reduced sharply â†’ true loss surfacing  
________________________________________  
### Required Underwriting Actions  
- Mumbai:  
o	Rate increase  
o	Portfolio pruning  
o	Strict selection + deductibles  
o	Reinsurance redesign  
- **SME**:  
o	Re-evaluate pricing adequacy  
o	Tighten underwriting filters  
- Delhi/Kolkata:  
o	Expense discipline + commission control

## RM / Sales Perspective  
### Growth Quality  
High-quality growth  
- Bangalore: **NEP** up 35 â†’ 52 (+48%), claims collapsed â†’ excellent  
- Hyderabad: **NEP** doubled â†’ stable LR  
Poor-quality growth  
- Mumbai:  
o	**GWP** drop -32%, but losses exploded  
â†’ RMs previously chased scale without quality  
- Delhi:  
o	**GWP** +6%, **NEP** +17%  
o	UW result dropped 35 â†’ 11 (-69%)  
â†’ growth not profitable  
________________________________________  
Strategic RM Interpretation  
- Do **NOT** chase top-line blindly in large metros (Mumbai, Delhi)  
- Focus on:   
o	Bangalore-type accounts (better risk selection)  
o	Mid-size stable segments (Hyderabad, Chennai)  
________________________________________  
Startup / Emerging Strategy  
- **SME** vertical:   
o	**GWP** up +42%, but **COR** 94 â†’ **116** â†’ growth is loss-making  
âžˇď¸Ź Emerging/startups:  
- High acquisition cost  
- Weak pricing  
- Low scale advantage  
âś… Focus on:  
- Emerging-2 / Emerging-3 segments

- Risk: LR **253**%, **COR** **283**%  
- UW: De-risk immediately  
- RM: Stop volume push  
- Action: Portfolio pruning, pricing reset

## Key Risks and Red Flags  
- **NEP** collapse (-29%) masking true ratios  
- Dependency on PY reserves (**IBNR** drop -87%)  
- Expense ratio surge (+10 pts)  
- Mumbai catastrophic loss  
- **SME** growth = loss-making  
- Commission income collapse  
- Highly volatile claims patterns  
________________________________________  
## Recommended Management Actions  
Underwriting  
- Tighten Mumbai exposure immediately  
- Reprice **SME** segment  
- Introduce deductibles and stricter filters  
- Review RI structure  
RM / Distribution  
- Shift focus â†’ Bangalore, Hyderabad  
- Avoid low-quality metro growth  
- Segment-driven selling (avoid early startups)  
Portfolio  
- Reduce dependency on reinsurance commissions  
- Improve cost discipline  
- Rebalance towards Retail  
Data / Dashboard  
- Track **NEP** vs **GWP** conversion  
- Claims volatility by account size  
- Cost leakage monitoring  
________________________________________  
## Final Conclusion  
- Portfolio is deteriorating materially  
- Profitability in PY was inflated via reserves and RI income  
- Current year shows true underlying weakness  
- Growth quality is mixed and often poor  
- Retail and Bangalore-type segments should be scaled  
- Mumbai and **SME** need aggressive correction

## Key Portfolio Message  
- Portfolio has shifted from profitable (**COR** 81%) to loss-making (**COR** **115**%) despite only -6.6% decline in **GWP**.  
- Core issue = earnings compression + cost inflation, not just claims.  
- **NEP** dropped sharply (-29%), significantly weakening margin absorption capacity.  
- Expense ratio spike (40% â†’ 50%) is the largest driver of deterioration.  
- Profitability in Mar-25 was supported by RI commission and high **IBNR**, which is not repeating in Mar-26.  
- True underlying underwriting weakness is now visible.  
- Performance is highly polarized:   
o	Strong improvements: Bangalore, Retail  
o	Severe collapse: Mumbai  
- Growth quality is inconsistent and often poor (especially **SME**, Delhi, Mumbai).  
________________________________________  
## Underwriting Message  
- Portfolio profitability is not structurally stable:  
o	**IBNR** reduced 87%, exposing underlying loss trends  
o	RI commission dropped -24%, removing buffer income  
- Claims are not the main issue â†’ cost + earnings compression is  
o	Claims â†“ 38%, but LR worsened due to **NEP** decline  
- Major underwriting risks identified:  
o	Mumbai: catastrophic deterioration (**COR** **283**%)  
o	**SME** vertical: structurally loss-making (**COR** **116**%)  
o	Expense leakage across locations (+10 pts overall)  
- Positive underwriting signals:  
o	Bangalore turnaround (**COR** **249**% â†’ 53%)  
o	Retail normalization (**COR** **149**% â†’ 84%)  
o	Corporate segment remains stable (**COR** 55%)  
- Portfolio classification:  
o	Scale: Bangalore, Retail  
o	Selective growth: Chennai, Hyderabad  
o	Monitor: Delhi, Kolkata  
o	Correct / De-risk: Mumbai, **SME**  
________________________________________  
## RM Message  
- Top-line growth â‰  value creation  
o	Delhi: +**GWP** but UW profit down 69%  
o	**SME**: +42% growth but loss-making  
- High-quality growth pockets:  
o	Bangalore (strong **NEP** growth + low LR)  
o	Hyderabad (balanced growth, stable **COR**)  
o	Retail segment (profit turnaround)  
- Low-quality / destructive growth:  
o	Mumbai (massive underwriting loss despite past scale)  
o	**SME**/startup-heavy deals (high cost, weak margins)  
- Key RM implications:  
o	Shift from volume push â†’ margin-led selling  
o	Focus on mid-sized stable accounts (Emerging-2/3, **SME** mature)  
o	Avoid early-stage startup / price-sensitive deals  
- RM prioritization:  
o	Push: Bangalore, Hyderabad  
o	Selective: Chennai, Delhi  
o	Avoid aggressive growth: Mumbai, **SME**-heavy portfolios  
________________________________________  
## Top 5 Strengths  
## Retail segment turnaround: UW result -45 â†’ +19 (+64), COR improved 149% â†’ 84%  
## Bangalore recovery: UW -52 â†’ +26 (+78), LR dropped 213% â†’ 13%  
## Corporate segment stability: COR maintained at ~55% despite scale  
## Absolute claims reduced: NIC -38%, indicating improved experience or mix  
## Hyderabad steady growth: NEP doubled with stable COR (~75%)  
________________________________________  
## Top 5 Concerns  
## Portfolio flipped to loss: UW result +69 â†’ -35 (-104), COR 81% â†’ 115%  
## Mumbai collapse: UW +119 â†’ -94 (-213), COR 283%, LR 253%  
## Expense ratio surge: 40% â†’ 50% (+10 pts) despite lower GWP  
## NEP contraction: -29%, significantly weakening earnings base  
## SME segment loss-making: COR 116%, growth is unprofitable  
________________________________________  
## Immediate Actions  
Underwriting  
- Mumbai: Immediate portfolio pruning, pricing reset, stricter risk selection  
- **SME**: Reprice and tighten underwriting filters (especially early-stage risks)  
- Expense control: Enforce location-level cost discipline  
RM / Distribution  
- Redirect growth to:   
o	Bangalore  
o	Hyderabad  
o	Retail segment  
- Stop volume-driven acquisition in weak segments (Mumbai/**SME**)  
- Incentivize profit-linked sales, not premium volume  
### Portfolio Management  
- Reduce reliance on RI commission-driven profitability  
- Rebalance mix toward Retail + stable Corporate accounts  
- Monitor **NEP** conversion rigorously

## Key Portfolio Message  
- Portfolio delivered hyper growth (**GWP** +**109**%) but deepened losses (UW: -**353** â†’ -**494**, -41%) â†’ growth is structurally unprofitable.  
- **COR** improved from **235**% to **170**% (-65 pts), but still severely loss-making.  
- **NEP** surged **207** â†’ **566** (+**173**%), but claims scaled disproportionately (**NIC** +65%), keeping LR >**100**%.  
- Incurred LR improved (**152**% â†’ **102**%), but remains above break-even, indicating systemic pricing inadequacy.  
- Expense ratio reduced marginally (65% â†’ 61%) but absolute costs doubled (+99%), indicating scale without efficiency.  
- Retail and Delhi are primary growth drivers but key loss contributors.  
- Corporate segment turned around sharply (**COR** **346**% â†’ 98%) â†’ potential scalable segment.  
- **SME** Broking and Emerging segments deteriorated significantly â†’ poor-quality growth pockets.  
- Portfolio still dependent on scale rather than underwriting discipline.  
- Claims experience + expense burden = dual pressure model, not sustainable.  
________________________________________  
## Underwriting Message  
- Portfolio shows clear structural underwriting weakness:  
o	LR still >**100**% (**102**%)  
o	**COR** still **170**% â†’ far from profitability  
- Premium inadequacy remains core issue:  
o	Claims growing +**243** vs **NEP** +**359** â†’ insufficient margin absorption  
- **IBNR** reduced (57 â†’ 35, -39%)  
â†’ Improvement partly reserve-driven; sustainability risk  
- Major underwriting stress locations:  
o	Delhi: **COR** worsened **189**% â†’ **195**%  
o	Mumbai: **COR** still **288**%  
o	Hyderabad: **COR** ~**196**% with **100**% LR + **107**% expense  
- Strong underwriting improvements:  
o	Bangalore: **COR** **149**% â†’ 55%  
o	Corporate vertical: **COR** **346**% â†’ 98%  
- Underwriting classification:  
o	Scale: Bangalore, Corporate  
o	Selective: Ahmedabad, Pune  
o	Monitor: Kolkata, Indore  
o	Correct: Chennai, Delhi  
o	De-risk: Mumbai, **SME** Broking, Hyderabad  
________________________________________  
## RM Message  
- Growth quality highly inconsistent:  
o	Delhi **GWP** +**618** (+**108**%), but UW loss worsened -94 â†’ -**233**  
o	Retail **GWP** +1,**114** (+**108**%), but UW loss expanded -**245** â†’ -**352**  
- High-quality RM contribution:  
o	Bangalore: **GWP** +**182**%, UW -5 â†’ +5  
o	Corporate: **GWP** +**149**%, near breakeven UW  
- Low-quality growth pockets:  
o	**SME** Broking: **GWP** +67% but **COR** **314**%  
o	Emerging: **GWP** +**101**% but **COR** **162**%  
- RM implication:  
o	Current strategy over-emphasizes volume vs margin  
o	Acquisition cost stable (~18%) but not delivering profitability  
- RM prioritization:  
o	Push: Corporate, Bangalore  
o	Selective: Pune, Ahmedabad  
o	Avoid blind growth: Delhi, **SME** Broking, Emerging  
o	De-prioritize: Mumbai  
________________________________________  
## Top 5 Strengths  
## Massive scale expansion: GWP +1,668 (+109%), strong market traction  
## Corporate turnaround: COR 346% â†’ 98%, UW loss nearly eliminated  
## Bangalore profitability shift: COR 149% â†’ 55%, UW positive  
## Loss ratio improvement: 152% â†’ 102% (-50 pts)  
## Pune and Ahmedabad showing improving loss experience  
________________________________________  
## Top 5 Concerns  
## Absolute underwriting loss worsening: -353 â†’ -494 (-141)  
## Portfolio still deeply loss-making (COR 170%)  
## Delhi driving scale but also losses: UW -233, COR 195%  
## SME Broking collapse: COR 243% â†’ 314%, LR 232%  
## Expense base doubled (221 â†’ 440) â†’ poor operating leverage  
________________________________________  
## Immediate Actions  
Underwriting  
- Reprice aggressively in loss-heavy segments (**SME**, Emerging, Delhi, Mumbai)  
- Introduce deductibles / stricter selection filters  
- Reduce exposure to persistently high LR zones (>**150**%)  
RM / Distribution  
- Shift from volume-driven to margin-driven incentives  
- Prioritize:   
o	Corporate accounts  
o	Bangalore-type portfolios  
- Reduce acquisition in:   
o	**SME** Broking  
o	Emerging early-stage  
### Portfolio Management  
- Rebalance mix toward Corporate + stable Retail pockets  
- Control expense escalation â†’ improve cost-to-**NEP** efficiency  
## Key Portfolio Message  
- **MSME** Suraksha Kavach is scaling fast, but the growth remains loss-making.  
- **GWP** increased from 1,**536** to 3,**204** (+1,**668**, +**109**%), while underwriting loss deepened from -**353** to -**494** (-**141**, -40%).  
- Portfolio **COR** improved from **235**% to **170**% (-65 pts), but this is still far above profitability threshold.  
- **NEP** grew sharply from **207** to **566** (+**359**, +**173**%), but **NIC** After **IBNR** also increased from **371** to **614** (+**243**, +65%), keeping the book structurally adverse.  
- Incurred LR improved from **152**% to **102**% (-50 pts), but at **102**% the earned premium is still insufficient to absorb claims, before expenses.  
- Expense ratio improved marginally from 65% to 61% (-4 pts), but expense outgo nearly doubled from **221** to **440** (+**219**, +99%).  
- The portfolio is improving from an extremely weak base, but it is not yet commercially viable.  
________________________________________  
## Underwriting Message  
- Core issue remains pricing and portfolio quality, not just scale.  
- Even after strong premium growth, the portfolio still reports:   
o	LR above **100**%  
o	**COR** at **170**%  
o	UW loss of -**494**  
- Claims remain the principal pressure point:   
o	**NIC** After **IBNR** increased from **371** to **614** (+**243**, +65%)  
o	Despite LR improvement, the claims burden remains too high relative to earned premium  
- Reserve support is lower:   
o	**IBNR** reduced from 57 to 35 (-22, -39%)  
o	This suggests the reported improvement is not being driven by reserve strengthening, which is positive, but also means the remaining loss experience is more â€śrealâ€ť and less cushioned  
- Best underwriting movement:   
o	Corporate vertical: **COR** improved from **346**% to 98%  
o	Bangalore: **COR** improved from **149**% to 55%  
- Worst underwriting pressure:   
o	Mumbai: **COR** still **288**%  
o	Delhi: **COR** worsened from **189**% to **195**%  
o	**SME** Broking: **COR** deteriorated from **243**% to **314**%  
- Underwriting view: the book needs selective scaling, not broad-based growth.  
________________________________________  
## RM Message  
- Sales success is not translating into profitable growth.  
- Several large growth pockets are commercially weak:   
o	Delhi **GWP** grew from **571** to 1,**189** (+**618**, +**108**%), but UW loss worsened from -94 to -**233** (-**139**)  
o	Retail vertical **GWP** grew from 1,**029** to 2,**143** (+1,**114**, +**108**%), but UW loss deepened from -**245** to -**352** (-**107**)  
- High-quality RM growth exists, but it is selective:   
o	Bangalore: **GWP** 38 to **107** (+69, +**182**%), UW result -5 to +5  
o	Corporate: **GWP** **127** to **316** (+**189**, +**149**%), UW result improved from -45 to -2  
- Low-quality RM growth is visible in **SME** / Emerging pockets:   
o	**SME** Broking: **GWP** 63 to **105** (+42, +67%), **COR** worsened to **314**%  
o	Emerging: **GWP** **318** to **640** (+**322**, +**101**%), UW loss widened -45 to -91  
- RM implication:   
o	Stop rewarding premium volume in isolation  
o	Shift toward margin-led account selection  
o	Focus on renewal quality, pricing discipline, and account mix improvement  
________________________________________  
## Top 5 Strengths  
## Strong scale build-up  
o	**GWP** increased by +1,**668** (+**109**%)  
o	Demonstrates strong market acceptance and distribution reach  
## Material LR improvement  
o	Incurred LR reduced from **152**% to **102**% (-50 pts)  
o	Indicates improvement in underlying claims ratio, though still inadequate  
## Corporate segment turnaround  
o	**COR** improved from **346**% to 98% (-**248** pts)  
o	UW loss reduced from -45 to -2 (+43)  
## Bangalore emerged as a profitable growth pocket  
o	**COR** improved from **149**% to 55%  
o	UW result improved from -5 to +5  
## Expense ratio improved modestly despite scale expansion  
o	Expense ratio reduced from 65% to 61% (-4 pts)  
o	Suggests some operating leverage, although absolute cost remains high  
________________________________________  
## Top 5 Concerns  
## Portfolio remains deeply loss-making  
o	UW loss worsened from -**353** to -**494** (-**141**, -40%)  
## Combined Ratio still unsustainably high  
o	**COR** at **170**%, despite a 65-point improvement  
## Delhi is scaling aggressively but destroying value  
o	**GWP** +**108**%, UW loss worsened to -**233**  
o	**COR** increased from **189**% to **195**%  
## Mumbai remains structurally broken  
o	**COR** improved from **344**% to **288**%, but still catastrophic  
o	Expense ratio surged from 52% to 92%  
## SME Broking and Emerging are poor-quality growth segments  
o	**SME** Broking **COR** worsened to **314**%  
o	Emerging **COR** worsened from **153**% to **162**%  
o	Both show expansion without profitability discipline  
________________________________________  
## Immediate Actions  
Underwriting  
- Reprice aggressively in Delhi, Mumbai, **SME** Broking, and Emerging segments  
- Tighten underwriting with:   
o	higher deductibles  
o	stronger referral controls  
o	stricter risk selection  
o	sharper renewal screening  
- Review whether current ceding structure is delivering enough protection relative to retained economics  
RM / Distribution  
- Shift RM focus from volume growth to profitable growth  
- Prioritise:   
o	Corporate  
o	Bangalore  
o	select better-performing retail pockets  
- De-emphasise new business push in:   
o	Mumbai  
o	Delhi (until pricing improves)  
o	**SME** Broking  
o	low-quality Emerging business  
### Portfolio Management  
- Rebalance mix toward better-performing segments and geographies  
- Monitor **NEP** growth versus claim growth more tightly  
- Introduce location / segment-level profitability gates before scaling further

Insights:  
Absolutely â€” adjusted for your clarification: there is only one Chennai, and the high-stress row is Delhi, not a second Chennai.  
Below is the fully re-adjusted analysis with that correction reflected throughout.  
________________________________________  
## Executive Summary  
- The Select Liability portfolio delivered strong top-line growth, with **GWP** increasing from 56 to 77 (+21, +37.5%), **NWP** from 45 to 61 (+16, +35.6%), and **NEP** from 31 to 50 (+19, +61.3%).  
- However, portfolio quality worsened materially. The clearest evidence is **COR** deteriorating from 29% to 46% (+17 pts) and underwriting margin falling from 58.1% to 46.0% (-12.1 pts).  
- Absolute underwriting result still improved from 18 to 23 (+5, +27.8%), but this is a volume-led improvement, not a quality-led one.  
- The single biggest issue is Delhi. Delhiâ€™s **GWP** doubled from 9 to 18 (+9, +**100**%), but **NIC** after **IBNR** rose from 0 to 7, UW result swung from +2 to -4 (-6), and **COR** exploded from 32% to **115**% (+83 pts). This is the clearest case of poor-quality growth.  
- On the location data provided, Delhi accounts for **100**% of visible **FY26** claims cost (7 out of total portfolio **NIC** after **IBNR** of 7).  
- The strongest scaled underwriting branches are Hyderabad, Bangalore, and Chennai:   
o	Hyd: **GWP** 13 to 15, **NEP** 7 to 11, UW 5 to 8, **COR** 16% to 19%  
o	Bangalore: **GWP** 11 to 18, **NEP** 6 to 11, UW 3 to 6, **COR** 33% to 32%  
o	Chennai: **GWP** 9 to 11, **NEP** 6 to 8, UW 4 to 6, **COR** 31% to 29%  
- Retail remains the dominant vertical, contributing 66 of 77 **GWP** (85.7%), 42 of 50 **NEP** (84.0%), and 17 of 23 UW result (73.9%) in **FY26**. That also means Retail is the main reason the aggregate portfolio answer matters.  
- Retail growth was not cleanly profitable. Retail **GWP** rose 47 to 66 (+19, +40.4%), but **COR** worsened from 28% to 50% (+22 pts), and the source shows loss ratio increasing from 0% to 16%.  
- **SME** Broking is the cleanest growth pocket in the visible data: **GWP** 2 to 5 (+**150**%), **NEP** 1 to 3 (+**200**%), UW 1 to 2 (+**100**%), **COR** 26% to 20% (-6 pts).  
- Reinsurance usage increased modestly: Prop ceding 2 to 3 (+50%), Non-prop 9 to 13 (+44.4%), while retention slipped from 80.4% to 79.2% (-1.1 pts). Reinsurance rose, but not enough to prevent the Delhi deterioration from hitting results.  
- Selling cost discipline weakened. Acquisition cost rose from 7 to 12 (+5, +71.4%), Acquisition cost % from 12% to 15% (+3 pts), and Commission ratio from 15% to 18% (+3 pts).  
- Expense ratio stayed flat at 15%, but absolute expense still rose from 7 to 9 (+2, +28.6%) because the book became larger.  
- There are important data-warning signals in the source itself:   
o	location totals do not fully reconcile to total (locations sum to 76 **GWP** in **FY26** vs total 77)  
o	location **NEP** sums to 51 vs total 50  
o	vertical **NEP** also sums to 51 vs total 50  
o	vertical **FY25** UW sums to 17 vs total 18  
o	Delhiâ€™s displayed LR is 74%, while 7 claims on 9 **NEP** implies 77.8%  
- Management should scale Hyderabad, Bangalore, Chennai, and **SME** Broking, hold / watch Ahmedabad, review cost-heavy smaller branches, and correct Delhi urgently before allowing any further aggressive growth.  
- Bottom line: the portfolio is still profitable, but underwriting quality has deteriorated. Growth is mixed â€” some of it is excellent, but Delhi and large parts of Retail have compromised quality.  
________________________________________  
## Overall Portfolio Analysis  
Premium movement  
- **GWP** increased from 56 to 77, an increase of 21 or 37.5%.  
- **NWP** increased from 45 to 61, an increase of 16 or 35.6%.  
- Growth at this pace is commercially attractive, but from an underwriting perspective, the issue is whether the added premium carried acceptable claims and cost quality. It did not fully do so.  
Retention / ceding movement  
- Retention ratio (**NWP**/**GWP**) declined from 80.36% (45/56) to 79.22% (61/77), a movement of -1.14 pts.  
- Ceding ratio increased from 19.64% to 20.78%, a rise of +1.14 pts.  
- Components:   
o	Prop ceding: 2 to 3 (+1, +50%)  
o	Non-prop: 9 to 13 (+4, +44.4%)  
- Interpretation:   
o	Reinsurance support increased, especially non-prop.  
o	However, the portfolio still took a visible underwriting hit in **FY26**, driven by claims emergence and higher selling cost.  
o	This suggests reinsurance was not the core driver of deterioration; the deterioration sat in underlying business quality, most visibly in Delhi.  
**NEP** movement  
- **NEP** increased from 31 to 50, an increase of 19 or 61.3%.  
- **NEP** grew much faster than **GWP**, meaning more premium was earned through P&L in **FY26**.  
- This amplifies two things:   
1. any good underwriting decisions show up faster in income;  
2. any claims deterioration also shows up more visibly.  
**URR** / earning pattern  
- PY **URR** increased from 14 to 28 (+14, +**100**%)  
- **URR** Charge increased from 52 to 72 (+20, +38.5%)  
- CY Release increased from 23 to 33 (+10, +43.5%)  
- Net **URR** impact (**URR** Charge - CY Release) moved from 29 to 39 (+10).  
- This suggests the book had a larger in-force premium base and more earning emergence. That helped lift **NEP**, but it also means the reported deterioration is not simply because the book was smaller or under-earned.  
Claims cost movement  
- **NIC** Before **IBNR** moved from 0 to 7  
- **IBNR** remained 0  
- **NIC** After **IBNR** moved from 0 to 7  
- This means the entire reported claims deterioration came from visible incurred claims, not reserve strengthening via **IBNR**.  
**IBNR** / reserve effect  
- Source shows **IBNR** = 0 in both years.  
- From a strict reporting perspective, that means the **FY26** deterioration was not reserve-loaded.  
- From a management perspective, because this is a liability line, zero **IBNR** together with fresh claims emergence deserves review. It may be correct in this extract, but it is not something to take comfort from without reserve validation.  
Loss ratio / incurred LR  
- Financial LR moved from 0% to 14%  
- Incurred LR moved from 0% to 14%  
- So the portfolio added 14 points of claims pressure year-on-year.  
- That is the single biggest ratio deterioration after Delhiâ€™s local branch shock.  
Expense ratio  
- Expense ratio remained flat at 15%  
- But Expense in Mns increased from 7 to 9 (+2, +28.6%)  
- So operating expense rose in absolute terms, but scale kept the ratio flat.  
- Flat expense ratio is not enough to offset what happened in claims and acquisition cost.  
Acquisition cost %  
- Acquisition cost increased from 7 to 12 (+5, +71.4%)  
- Acquisition Cost % increased from 12% to 15% (+3 pts)  
- This is a meaningful deterioration in selling efficiency.  
Commission ratio  
- Commission ratio increased from 15% to 18% (+3 pts)  
- Higher commission ratio plus higher acquisition cost % indicates the **FY26** growth came through a more expensive distribution mix and/or weaker pricing discipline.  
Underwriting result  
- UW Result increased from 18 to 23 (+5, +27.8%)  
- But this is not as positive as it looks, because:   
o	**NEP** increased 61.3%  
o	UW profit increased only 27.8%  
o	Hence underwriting profit per unit of **NEP** has weakened.  
Underwriting margin  
- UW margin on **NEP** fell from 58.06% (18/31) to 46.00% (23/50), a decline of 12.06 pts.  
- This is one of the cleanest indicators that quality deteriorated, even though absolute profit is up.  
Combined ratio  
- **COR** worsened from 29% to 46% (+17 pts)  
- A 17-point deterioration is significant and confirms that the **FY26** book is less profitable in ratio quality than **FY25**.  
Whether overall portfolio quality improved or worsened  
Overall portfolio quality worsened.  
The reasons are clear:  
- Incurred LR: 0% to 14%  
- Acquisition Cost %: 12% to 15%  
- Commission Ratio: 15% to 18%  
- **COR**: 29% to 46%  
- UW Margin: 58.1% to 46.0%  
So the portfolio is bigger and still profitable, but less clean and less resilient.  
________________________________________  
## Underwriting Perspective  
Underwriting profitability quality  
The portfolio remains profit-making, but the quality of the underwriting result has weakened.  
- **FY25**: UW result 18 on 31 **NEP** = 58.1% UW margin  
- **FY26**: UW result 23 on 50 **NEP** = 46.0% UW margin  
This tells you:  
- profitability still exists;  
- however, the incremental business written in **FY26** was lower quality than the existing portfolio.  
That is exactly the type of situation where management can make the mistake of celebrating top-line and absolute profit while missing the fact that margins are compressing underneath.  
Premium adequacy versus claims  
At aggregate level, the portfolio still appears adequately priced because:  
- **COR** is 46%, still comfortably below **100**%  
- UW result is +23  
But adequacy is not uniform. One pocket is clearly underpriced and/or structurally weak:  
Delhi  
- **GWP**: 9 to 18 (+**100**%)  
- **NEP**: 5 to 9 (+80%)  
- **NIC** After **IBNR**: 0 to 7  
- Displayed LR / Incurred LR: 74%  
- Implied LR on **NEP**: 7/9 = 77.8%  
- Acq Cost %: 17% to 23%  
- Commission Ratio: 20% to 28%  
- Expense Ratio: 11% to 13%  
- **COR**: 32% to **115**%  
- UW Result: +2 to -4  
This is not a minor fluctuation. It is a classic example of non-remunerative growth:  
- premium doubled,  
- claims emerged sharply,  
- pricing/cost terms worsened,  
- underwriting turned negative.  
Reserve dependence  
- There is no visible reserve dependence in the source numbers because **IBNR** stayed at 0.  
- That said, from an underwriting governance standpoint, this is also a risk: liability lines usually need reserve caution, especially when loss activity has appeared.  
Geographies causing stress  
Delhi â€” the primary underwriting problem  
Delhi is the most important issue in the location view.  
Why Delhi matters:  
- It contributed 9 of the total 21 **GWP** increase (42.9%)  
- It contributed 4 of the total 19 **NEP** increase (21.1%)  
- It contributed -6 of the total +5 UW change, i.e. negative **120**% of portfolio UW change  
- It carries **100**% of visible location-level claims emergence in **FY26**  
This means that without Delhi, the visible branch book would look dramatically stronger.  
Smaller cost-heavy branches  
These are not yet catastrophic, but they are not attractive either:  
Indore  
- **GWP** 0 to 1  
- **NEP** flat at 1  
- UW flat at 0  
- **COR** 39% to 50%  
- Acq Cost % 24% to 25%  
- Commission 29% to 30%  
- Expense 10% to 20%  
- No claims, but still weak economics.  
Pune  
- **GWP** 3 to 4 (+33.3%)  
- **NEP** 1 to 2 (+**100**%)  
- UW 0 to 1  
- **COR** 45% to 44%  
- Acq Cost % 22% to 25%  
- Commission 27% to 30%  
- Profitable, but expensive.  
Kolkata  
- **GWP** 1 to 2 (+**100**%)  
- UW 0 to 1  
- **COR** 47% to 46%  
- Acq Cost % 14% to 19%  
- Commission 16% to 23%  
- Small book, middling economics.  
Mumbai  
- **GWP** 6 to 3 (-50%)  
- **NEP** 3 to 4 (+33.3%)  
- UW 1 to 3 (+2)  
- **COR** 33% to 46% (+13 pts)  
- Acq Cost % 11% to 21%  
- Commission 12% to 28%  
- This is a contradictory branch: lower premium, higher **NEP**, better absolute UW, but much worse economics. It suggests mix distortion, timing effects, or run-off dynamics rather than reliably better underwriting.  
Geographies showing strong underwriting quality  
Hyderabad  
- **GWP** 13 to 15 (+15.4%)  
- **NEP** 7 to 11 (+57.1%)  
- UW 5 to 8 (+60%)  
- **COR** 16% to 19%  
- Acq Cost % 4% to 5%  
- Commission ratio 5% to 6%  
- Zero visible claims  
- This is the cleanest scaled underwriting branch in the book.  
Bangalore  
- **GWP** 11 to 18 (+63.6%)  
- **NEP** 6 to 11 (+83.3%)  
- UW 3 to 6 (+**100**%)  
- **COR** 33% to 32% (-1 pt)  
- Acq Cost % improved 16% to 12%  
- Commission improved 19% to 14%  
- Zero visible claims  
- Strong profitable growth.  
Chennai  
- **GWP** 9 to 11 (+22.2%)  
- **NEP** 6 to 8 (+33.3%)  
- UW 4 to 6 (+50%)  
- **COR** 31% to 29% (-2 pts)  
- Expense ratio improved 17% to 14%  
- Zero visible claims  
- Very attractive underwriting quality.  
Ahmedabad  
- Smaller scale, but decent:  
- **GWP** flat at 4  
- **NEP** 2 to 3 (+50%)  
- UW 1 to 2 (+**100**%)  
- **COR** 30% to 29%  
- But cost ratios worsened, so this is positive but not as clean as Bangalore / Hyd / Chennai.  
Verticals causing underwriting stress  
Retail  
Retail is the biggest underwriting strategic issue because of its scale:  
- **GWP** 47 to 66 (+19, +40.4%)  
- **NEP** 26 to 42 (+16, +61.5%)  
- UW 15 to 17 (+2, +13.3%)  
- **COR** 28% to 50% (+22 pts)  
- Displayed LR 0% to 16%  
- Acq Cost % 12% to 15% (+3 pts)  
- Commission ratio 14% to 18% (+4 pts)  
- Expense ratio 14% to 16% (+2 pts)  
Interpretation:  
- Retail is still profitable,  
- but the incremental Retail growth is much lower quality than the legacy book,  
- and because Retail is 85.7% of **GWP**, it effectively dictates portfolio quality.  
Emerging  
- **GWP** 5 to 4 (-20%)  
- **NEP** 3 to 4 (+33.3%)  
- UW 1 to 2  
- **COR** 42% to 43%  
- Acq Cost % 21% to 26%  
- Commission 25% to 31%  
- No claims, but expensive and not commercially compelling.  
Verticals showing strong underwriting quality  
**SME** Broking  
- **GWP** 2 to 5 (+**150**%)  
- **NEP** 1 to 3 (+**200**%)  
- UW 1 to 2 (+**100**%)  
- **COR** 26% to 20% (-6 pts)  
- Acq Cost % 8% to 10%  
- Commission 9% to 11%  
- Expense ratio 18% to 8%  
- Best visible growth-quality vertical.  
Corp  
- **GWP** flat at 2  
- **NEP** 1 to 2  
- UW 0 to 2  
- **COR** 30% to 7%  
- However, expense ratio is shown at -9%, which is a clear data anomaly.  
- So Corp looks strong, but management should not take strategic direction from it until the expense line is validated.  
Sustainable vs volatile business  
Sustainable  
- Hyderabad  
- Bangalore  
- Chennai  
- **SME** Broking These show acceptable scale / growth with stable or improved profitability and no visible claims deterioration.  
Volatile / unstable  
- Delhi  
- Retail (because of scale-driven deterioration)  
- Mumbai (contradictory profile)  
- Small high-cost branches like Indore, Pune, Kolkata  
Where underwriting appetite should be expanded  
- Hyderabad  
- Bangalore  
- Chennai  
- **SME** Broking  
- Selective Ahmedabad  
Where underwriting appetite should be tightened  
- Delhi â€” immediate tightening  
- Retail pockets resembling Delhi profile  
- Emerging, unless pricing/cost structure improves  
- Indore / Pune / Kolkata / Mumbai where acquisition/commission load is high for the scale  
Pricing / deductible / wording / referral / reinsurance implications  
- Pricing   
o	Delhi needs immediate repricing. A branch with 74% displayed LR, 23% Acq Cost %, 28% commission, and **115**% **COR** cannot be sustained on current rates.  
- Deductibles   
o	Increase deductibles / retentions in the risk pockets driving Delhiâ€™s claims.  
- Wording   
o	Review liability triggers, defence cost treatment, extensions, and sub-limits.  
- Referral   
o	Make Delhi-like risks referral-mandatory for specific industries, premium bands, or claim-prone occupations.  
- Reinsurance   
o	Review whether current treaty structure and attachment are appropriate for this product, especially where a single geography is creating all visible claims emergence.  
Classification of major areas  
Scale aggressively  
- Hyderabad  
- Bangalore  
- **SME** Broking  
Grow selectively  
- Chennai  
- Ahmedabad  
- Corp (only after data validation)  
Hold / monitor  
- Pune  
- Kolkata  
- Emerging  
Correct urgently  
- Delhi  
- Retail vertical  
De-risk / tighten  
- Indore  
- Mumbai  
- Any business carrying high claims + high commission + high acquisition cost

## RM / Sales / Distribution Perspective  
Where growth is healthy  
Bangalore  
- **GWP** +7 (+63.6%)  
- **NEP** +5 (+83.3%)  
- UW +3 (+**100**%)  
- **COR** improved from 33% to 32%  
- This is exactly what an RM head wants: growth with stable economics.  
Hyderabad  
- **GWP** +2 (+15.4%)  
- **NEP** +4 (+57.1%)  
- UW +3 (+60%)  
- **COR** remains only 19%  
- Low selling cost and strong profitability justify pushing this branch harder.  
Chennai  
- **GWP** +2 (+22.2%)  
- **NEP** +2 (+33.3%)  
- UW +2 (+50%)  
- **COR** improved from 31% to 29%  
- Strong quality growth with manageable cost structure.  
**SME** Broking  
- **GWP** +3 (+**150**%)  
- **NEP** +2 (+**200**%)  
- UW +1 (+**100**%)  
- **COR** improved from 26% to 20%  
- This is the strongest vertical from an RM growth-quality standpoint.  
Where growth is poor quality  
Delhi  
- **GWP** +9 (+**100**%)  
- **NEP** +4 (+80%)  
- UW -6  
- **COR** +83 pts to **115**%  
- Displayed LR = 74%  
- This is volume without value.  
Retail  
- **GWP** +19 (+40.4%)  
- **NEP** +16 (+61.5%)  
- UW +2 only  
- **COR** +22 pts to 50%  
- Strong growth, but much weaker quality. RMs should not be rewarded on volume alone here.  
Where RMs should push more business  
- Hyderabad  
- Bangalore  
- Chennai  
- **SME** Broking  
- Ahmedabad, but only under stricter commission discipline  
Where RMs should avoid chasing top-line  
- Delhi  
- Retail segments similar to Delhi  
- Indore  
- Mumbai, until economics stabilize  
- Pune / Kolkata unless lower-cost business can be sourced  
Whether acquisition cost is justified  
Portfolio-level answer: not fully.  
Why:  
- Acq Cost % rose from 12% to 15%  
- Commission ratio rose from 15% to 18%  
- Yet portfolio quality worsened.  
Therefore, extra acquisition spend is justified only where it is buying profitable business:  
- Bangalore  
- Hyderabad  
- Chennai  
- **SME** Broking  
It is not justified in:  
- Delhi  
- Indore  
- Pune  
- likely parts of Retail  
- Mumbai in its current form  
Which segments / geographies look attractive  
- Hyderabad  
- Bangalore  
- Chennai  
- **SME** Broking  
- Corp may be attractive, but the expense anomaly means it should be validated first.  
Where strategy should shift from volume to quality  
- Delhi  
- Retail overall  
- Mumbai  
- Emerging  
- Small branches with Acq Cost % above ~19% and Commission above ~23%  
Where cross-sell / up-sell / renewal focus may help  
- Hyd / Bangalore / Chennai   
o	strong candidate branches for wallet-share expansion and higher attachment  
- Ahmedabad   
o	selective cross-sell with tighter sales-cost controls  
- Mumbai   
o	focus on renewal remediation, not fresh volume  
- Retail   
o	renewal repricing and selective up-sell only into the better-performing micro-pockets

## Deep Dive by All Visible Groupings  
- Location-wise  
Ahmedabad  
- One-line summary: Stable branch with improved underwriting outcome, but sales costs have inflated.  
- Top positive: UW result 1 to 2 (+**100**%) and **COR** 30% to 29%  
- Top concern: Acq Cost % 12% to 19% (+7 pts) and Commission 15% to 23% (+8 pts)  
- Underwriting interpretation: Risk quality appears fine; cost structure is worsening faster than desirable.  
- RM interpretation: Growth is acceptable, but commission discipline must improve.  
- Exact reason using figures: **GWP** flat at 4, **NEP** 2 to 3 (+50%), no visible claims, expense ratio improves 16% to 5%, offsetting cost increase.  
- Recommended action: Grow selectively  
Bangalore  
- One-line summary: One of the best branches in the book â€” large, growing, and disciplined.  
- Top positive: **GWP** 11 to 18 (+63.6%), **NEP** 6 to 11 (+83.3%), UW 3 to 6 (+**100**%)  
- Top concern: Expense ratio 13% to 18% (+5 pts)  
- Underwriting interpretation: Strong clean growth with better sales-cost efficiency.  
- RM interpretation: This is a branch to back confidently.  
- Exact reason using figures: Acq Cost % improves 16% to 12%, Commission improves 19% to 14%, **COR** improves 33% to 32%, claims remain 0.  
- Recommended action: Scale aggressively  
Chennai  
- One-line summary: Clean profitable growth with improving underwriting quality.  
- Top positive: UW 4 to 6 (+50%), **COR** 31% to 29%  
- Top concern: Only modest concern is slight increase in helping costs: Acq Cost % 12% to 13%, Commission 14% to 15%  
- Underwriting interpretation: Very solid branch with sustainable underwriting quality.  
- RM interpretation: Attractive branch for controlled expansion.  
- Exact reason using figures: **GWP** 9 to 11 (+22.2%), **NEP** 6 to 8 (+33.3%), claims stay 0, expense ratio improves 17% to 14%  
- Recommended action: Grow selectively / near-aggressive  
Delhi  
- One-line summary: Fastest-growing major branch and the single biggest underwriting problem.  
- Top positive: Large top-line growth only: **GWP** 9 to 18 (+**100**%)  
- Top concern: UW +2 to -4, **COR** 32% to **115**%, Displayed LR 74%  
- Underwriting interpretation: This business is not currently priced or structured adequately.  
- RM interpretation: Stop rewarding this branch for volume; it is destroying profitability.  
- Exact reason using figures: **NEP** 5 to 9 (+80%), **NIC** after **IBNR** 0 to 7, Acq Cost % 17% to 23%, Commission 20% to 28%, Expense 11% to 13%  
- Recommended action: Correct urgently  
Indore  
- One-line summary: Tiny book with no claims, but weak economics.  
- Top positive: No visible claims.  
- Top concern: **COR** 39% to 50% despite no claims.  
- Underwriting interpretation: Cost-heavy and not yet scalable.  
- RM interpretation: Avoid volume-chasing until economics improve.  
- Exact reason using figures: Acq Cost % 24% to 25%, Commission 29% to 30%, Expense 10% to 20%  
- Recommended action: De-risk / tighten  
Hyd  
- One-line summary: Best quality scaled branch in the portfolio.  
- Top positive: UW 5 to 8 (+60%), **COR** only 19%  
- Top concern: Minor ratio drift up from 16% to 19%  
- Underwriting interpretation: Excellent branch with room to grow.  
- RM interpretation: High-quality growth engine.  
- Exact reason using figures: **GWP** 13 to 15 (+15.4%), **NEP** 7 to 11 (+57.1%), claims 0, Acq Cost % only 5%, Commission only 6%  
- Recommended action: Scale aggressively  
Kol  
- One-line summary: Small branch improving gradually, but still only average economics.  
- Top positive: **GWP** 1 to 2 (+**100**%), UW 0 to 1  
- Top concern: Acq Cost % 14% to 19%, Commission 16% to 23%  
- Underwriting interpretation: No claims, but cost load is too high for a tiny book.  
- RM interpretation: Grow only on better terms.  
- Exact reason using figures: **COR** 47% to 46%, expense ratio improves 30% to 23%, but cost structure remains high.  
- Recommended action: Hold / monitor  
Mum  
- One-line summary: Shrinking top-line with worsening economics and contradictory profit signals.  
- Top positive: UW 1 to 3  
- Top concern: **GWP** 6 to 3 (-50%) while **COR** 33% to 46%  
- Underwriting interpretation: Book mix likely worsened; apparent UW uplift is not enough to trust.  
- RM interpretation: Repair the portfolio first; do not chase fresh premium.  
- Exact reason using figures: Acq Cost % 11% to 21%, Commission 12% to 28%, no visible claims, expense ratio slightly better 20% to 18%  
- Recommended action: De-risk / tighten  
Pune  
- One-line summary: Small profitable branch, but too expensive relative to scale.  
- Top positive: **COR** 45% to 44%, UW 0 to 1  
- Top concern: Acq Cost % 22% to 25%, Commission 27% to 30%  
- Underwriting interpretation: Positive but not attractive enough to scale without cost correction.  
- RM interpretation: Better to improve quality than push volume.  
- Exact reason using figures: **GWP** 3 to 4 (+33.3%), **NEP** 1 to 2 (+**100**%), no claims, modest ratio improvement only.  
- Recommended action: Hold / monitor

## Key Risks and Red Flags  
- Margin compression: UW margin fell from 58.06% to 46.00% (-12.06 pts)  
- Adverse claims emergence: Incurred LR rose from 0% to 14%  
- Expense pressure: Expense ratio flat at 15%, but expense amount rose 7 to 9 (+28.6%)  
- Reserve dependence / reserve visibility concern: **IBNR** remains 0 despite **FY26** claims emergence  
- Unstable profitability: Delhi moved from +2 UW to -4 UW  
- Poor acquisition efficiency: Acq Cost % 12% to 15%, Commission 15% to 18%  
- Weak retention quality: Retention slipped 80.36% to 79.22%  
- Unsustainable growth patterns: Delhi grew **100**% but turned sharply loss-making  
- Concentration risk: Retail is 85.7% of **GWP** and 84.0% of **NEP**  
- Data integrity risk:   
o	locations sum to 76 **GWP** in **FY26** vs total 77  
o	locations sum to 51 **NEP** vs total 50  
o	verticals sum to 51 **NEP** vs total 50  
o	vertical **FY25** UW sums to 17 vs total 18  
o	Corp shows -9% expense ratio  
o	Delhiâ€™s displayed LR 74% does not exactly reconcile with 7/9 **NEP** = 77.8%

## Recommended Actions  
Underwriting actions  
## Immediate Delhi remediation   
o	Freeze or cap fresh growth  
o	Mandatory referral for renewals and new risks  
o	Reprice aggressively  
o	Review deductibles, sub-limits, coverage wording, and sector mix  
## Expand appetite in proven profitable branches   
o	Hyd  
o	Bangalore  
o	Chennai  
o	**SME** Broking  
## Retail segmentation   
o	Split profitable Retail pockets from deteriorating ones  
o	Do not treat Retail as uniformly healthy  
## Reserve review   
o	Recheck **IBNR** / case reserve adequacy given liability nature of the line  
## Reinsurance review   
o	Test whether treaty structure is appropriately protecting the risk profile emerging in Delhi / Retail  
RM / distribution actions  
## Push growth in high-quality branches   
o	Bangalore  
o	Hyd  
o	Chennai  
o	**SME** Broking  
## Stop paying for poor-quality growth   
o	Tighten commission / acquisition discipline in Delhi, Mumbai, Indore, Pune, Emerging  
## Rework incentive structure   
o	Reward growth only when accompanied by acceptable **COR** / LR / UW result  
## Renewal focus   
o	Delhi: repricing, non-renewal of weak accounts where needed  
o	Mumbai: renewal quality repair, not top-line chasing  
## Cross-sell and deepening   
o	Hyd / Bangalore / Chennai should be the primary wallet-share expansion branches  
Portfolio management actions  
## Ring-fence Delhi  
## Rebalance away from deteriorating Retail pockets  
## Scale SME Broking as a diversification lever  
## Set portfolio guardrails   
o	max commission thresholds  
o	max acquisition cost thresholds  
o	referral triggers for sudden growth with LR deterioration  
## Report performance on earned premium and COR, not only GWP  
Data / dashboard actions  
## Reconcile branch totals to total portfolio  
## Reconcile vertical totals to total portfolio  
## Validate Delhi loss ratio versus underlying rupee values  
## Validate negative expense ratio in Corp  
## Add branch Ă— vertical Ă— RM Ă— broker drill-down  
## Track new business vs renewal profitability separately  
## Add claim emergence triangles / cohort views if available

## Final Conclusion  
Is the portfolio improving or deteriorating?  
Deteriorating in quality, though still profitable in absolute terms.  
Is growth profitable or poor quality?  
Mixed.  
- Profitable growth: Hyd, Bangalore, Chennai, **SME** Broking  
- Poor-quality growth: Delhi and material parts of Retail  
Which areas should be scaled?  
- Hyd  
- Bangalore  
- Chennai  
- **SME** Broking  
- Selective Ahmedabad  
Which areas should be corrected?  
- Delhi  
- Retail  
- Emerging / high-cost low-scale branches  
Which areas should be de-risked?  
- Delhi (immediate)  
- Mum  
- Indore  
- any business showing the Delhi pattern of high growth + claims emergence + high selling cost
