# INDUSTRIAL ALL RISK POLICY  


## Executive Summary  
- The Industrial All Risk portfolio was flat on top-line but sharply better on booked profitability: **GWP** declined from 6,**632** to 6,**603** (-29, -0.4%), but UW Result increased from **182** to **922** (+**740**, +**406**.6%) and **COR** improved from 84% to 26% (-58 pts).  
- However, the improvement in booked results is not supported by underlying claims performance. **NIC** Before **IBNR** increased from **578** to **911** (+**333**, +57.6%), and the reported Incurred LR increased from 49% to 73% (+24 pts). This is a material deterioration in the core loss experience.  
- The apparent profitability improvement is primarily reserve-driven, not underwriting-led. **IBNR** swung from +**621** to -**669** (-1,**290**), pulling **NIC** After **IBNR** down from 1,**199** to **241** (-**958**, -79.9%) and Financial Loss Ratio from **101**% to 19% (-82 pts).  
- Put differently: reported profitability improved because the book released reserves, while underlying incurred claims worsened materially. This is the single most important management message.  
- Reinsurance dependence remains very high. Ceding stayed above 81% in both years: 82.5% in **FY25** vs 81.9% in **FY26** (-0.6 pts). Retention improved slightly from 17.5% to 18.1% (+0.6 pts), but the book remains highly ceded.  
- Reinsurance economics weakened. RI Commission reduced from 1,**383** to 1,**235** (-**148**, -10.7%), and the Commission Ratio moved from -48% to -32% (+16 pts), meaning the reinsurance commission support to net economics reduced materially.  
- Cost pressure worsened despite flat top-line. Acquisition Cost increased from **824** to **847** (+23, +2.8%), Acquisition Cost % rose from 12% to 13% (+1 pt), and Expense Ratio increased from 32% to 39% (+7 pts) with Expense in Mns up from **368** to **469** (+**101**, +27.4%).  
- The largest location by far is Mumbai, contributing 2,**945** **GWP** (44.6% of total **FY26** **GWP**). Reported Mumbai profitability improved dramatically (UW -1,**083** to +1,**565**; **COR** **368**% to -**333**%), but this was entirely driven by an **IBNR** swing from +1,**473** to -1,**346** (-2,**819**). Underlying incurred LR in Mumbai actually worsened from 38% to 55% (+17 pts).  
- The largest genuine underwriting stress in the portfolio is Delhi. **GWP** increased from 1,**428** to 1,**485** (+57, +4.0%), but **NIC** After **IBNR** rose from 52 to **537** (+**485**, +**932**.7%), Incurred LR increased from 76% to **102**% (+26 pts), UW Result fell from +**323** to -**208** (-**531**), and **COR** deteriorated from 5% to **159**% (+**154** pts).  
- Ahmedabad also moved from exceptional profitability to severe booked loss: UW Result +**507** to -**340** (-**847**), **COR** -**270**% to **307**% (+**577** pts), driven mainly by **IBNR** moving from -**446** to +**377** (+**823**). This is a strong reserve-strengthening signal.  
- Pune is the sharpest deterioration on pure ratio stress: Incurred LR -1% to **346**% (+**347** pts), UW Result +57 to -**153** (-**210**), and **COR** -29% to **371**% (+**400** pts).  
- Hyderabad is the cleanest genuine improvement. Despite **GWP** falling from **351** to **318** (-33, -9.4%), **NEP** increased from 75 to 86 (+11, +14.7%), **NIC** After **IBNR** fell from 76 to 44 (-32, -42.1%), Incurred LR fell from **126**% to 36% (-90 pts), and UW Result improved from -9 to +23 (+32).  
- At vertical level, Corporate remains the core book with 5,**575** **GWP** (84.4% of **FY26** **GWP**), but quality weakened sharply: UW Result fell from **886** to **234** (-**652**, -73.6%), Incurred LR rose from 50% to 76% (+26 pts), and **COR** worsened from 10% to 76% (+66 pts).  
- Retail growth was poor-quality growth: **GWP** **590** to **750** (+**160**, +27.1%), but **NIC** After **IBNR** 20 to **128** (+**108**, +**540**%), Incurred LR 38% to 75% (+37 pts), UW Result +89 to -56 (-**145**), and **COR** 40% to **133**% (+93 pts).  
- **SME** Broking is the best visible vertical on genuine underwriting sustainability: **GWP** **218** to **232** (+14, +6.4%), **NEP** 48 to 73 (+25, +52.1%), Incurred LR improved from 36% to 32% (-4 pts), UW Result 24 to 25 (+1), and **COR** remained manageable at 67%.  
- Immediate management focus should be on:   
1. separating reserve-release gains from true underwriting improvement,  
2. correcting Delhi, Pune, Ahmedabad, and Retail,  
3. not over-reading Mumbaiâ€™s reported turnaround, and  
4. scaling Hyderabad and **SME** Broking selectively, while preserving Chennaiâ€™s growth quality.  
________________________________________  
## Overall Portfolio Analysis  
Premium movement  
- **GWP** reduced from 6,**632** to 6,**603** (-29, -0.4%), so the overall portfolio is essentially flat on gross written premium.  
- **NWP** increased from 1,**161** to 1,**196** (+35, +3.0%), which means net premium improved despite flat gross premium.  
- This is supported by a mild reduction in ceding:   
o	Prop Ceding: 5,**167** to 5,**146** (-21, -0.4%)  
o	Non-Prop: **304** to **262** (-42, -13.8%)  
- Business implication: the portfolio retained slightly more premium, but this improvement is small relative to the deterioration in underlying incurred claims.  
Retention / ceding movement  
- Retention ratio (**NWP** / **GWP**) improved from 17.5% to 18.1% (+0.6 pts).  
- Ceding ratio reduced from 82.5% to 81.9% (-0.6 pts).  
- This is directionally positive, but the portfolio remains extremely reinsurance-heavy, with more than four-fifths of **GWP** ceded in both years.  
- RI Commission reduced from 1,**383** to 1,**235** (-**148**, -10.7%), and Commission Ratio moved from -48% to -32% (+16 pts).  
- Interpretation: even though ceding reduced marginally, the net economics from reinsurance support worsened materially. The book got less RI commission benefit in **FY26**.  
**NEP** movement  
- **NEP** increased from 1,**189** to 1,**244** (+55, +4.6%).  
- This is supported by:   
o	PY **URR**: **472** to **444** (-28, -5.9%)  
o	**URR** Charge: 1,**459** to 1,**454** (-5, -0.3%)  
o	CY Release: 1,**015** to 1,**058** (+43, +4.2%)  
- Business implication: more premium was earned in **FY26** despite flat **GWP**, which should normally support profitability. However, the underlying claims burden deteriorated faster than **NEP** growth.  
Claims movement  
The critical insight is that the portfolio shows a sharp divergence between underlying claims and booked claims.  
Underlying claims  
- **NIC** Before **IBNR** increased from **578** to **911** (+**333**, +57.6%)  
- Incurred LR increased from 49% to 73% (+24 pts)  
Booked claims after reserves  
- **IBNR** moved from +**621** to -**669** (-1,**290**)  
- **NIC** After **IBNR** dropped from 1,**199** to **241** (-**958**, -79.9%)  
- Financial Loss Ratio dropped from **101**% to 19% (-82 pts)  
Interpretation  
This strongly indicates:  
- underlying claims emergence worsened materially  
- booked claims fell only because reserves were released / reversed  
- management should therefore be careful not to interpret **FY26** as a true underwriting recovery  
This is not a subtle point; it is the central diagnostic of the portfolio.  
**IBNR** / reserve effect  
- **IBNR** swing = -1,**290** from +**621** to -**669**  
- This is extraordinarily large relative to:   
o	**NEP** = 1,**244**  
o	UW Result = **922**  
- A reserve movement of this size is large enough to dominate the yearâ€™s result.  
- Possible interpretation based on available data: the portfolio experienced a major reserve release / strengthening reversal in **FY26**, especially concentrated in Mumbai, where **IBNR** moved from +1,**473** to -1,**346** (-2,**819**).  
- This means the **FY26** underwriting result is highly reserve-dependent.  
Loss ratio / incurred LR  
- Reported Financial Loss Ratio improved from **101**% to 19% (-82 pts)  
- Reported Incurred LR worsened from 49% to 73% (+24 pts)  
This appears contradictory until we infer the reporting logic:  
- Incurred LR appears aligned to **NIC** Before **IBNR** / **NEP**  
- Financial Loss Ratio appears aligned to **NIC** After **IBNR** / **NEP**  
That means:  
- core claims experience got worse  
- booked claims ratio improved because reserve treatment turned favorable  
This is the single biggest contradiction and red flag in the dataset.  
Expense ratio  
- Expense Ratio increased from 32% to 39% (+7 pts)  
- Expense in Mns increased from **368** to **469** (+**101**, +27.4%)  
- This is a significant deterioration.  
- Since **GWP** was flat and **NEP** rose only 4.6%, but expense rose 27.4%, the portfolio suffered clear cost inflation and/or poor scale absorption.  
Acquisition cost ratio  
- Acquisition Cost increased from **824** to **847** (+23, +2.8%)  
- Acq Cost % increased from 12% to 13% (+1 pt)  
- This is deterioration, although much milder than the increase in expense ratio.  
- Across a reinsurance-heavy book, this still matters because net margin is already thin and volatile.  
Commission ratio  
- Commission Ratio moved from -48% to -32% (+16 pts)  
- Given the negative sign, this indicates less favorable commission economics, likely from lower RI commission support and/or weaker net outbound commission position.  
- Combined with RI Comm down by **148**, this is a clear drag on net underwriting profitability.  
Underwriting result  
- UW Result improved from **182** to **922** (+**740**, +**406**.6%)  
- On the face of it, this looks excellent.  
- But it is not supported by:   
o	underlying claims (Incurred LR worsened 49% to 73%)  
o	expense ratio (32% to 39%)  
o	acquisition ratio (12% to 13%)  
o	commission ratio (worsened by 16 pts)  
- Therefore, the underwriting result improvement is not a clean underwriting quality improvement; it is predominantly reserve-driven.  
Combined ratio  
- **COR** improved from 84% to 26% (-58 pts)  
- Again, this is not corroborated by the underlying ratio stack.  
- Since underlying incurred claims worsened and expenses rose sharply, the **COR** improvement is almost certainly the result of the **IBNR** release.  
- So the **FY26** **COR** is not a reliable indicator of sustainable forward profitability.  
Overall portfolio quality: improving or worsening?  
Reported profitability:  
- Improved sharply  
Underlying underwriting quality:  
- Worsened  
Final portfolio-level view:  
The portfolio is reportedly much more profitable, but underlying underwriting quality has deteriorated, and the **FY26** outcome is heavily reserve-dependent. Management should therefore treat the improvement as accounting-supported rather than fully operating-supported.  
________________________________________  
## Underwriting Perspective  
Portfolio profitability quality  
The portfolio remains apparently profitable in **FY26**, but the quality of that profitability is weak.  
- UW Margin on **NEP** rose from 15.3% (**182** / 1,**189**) to 74.1% (**922** / 1,**244**).  
- However, this increase is inconsistent with:   
o	Incurred LR rising from 49% to 73%  
o	Expense Ratio rising from 32% to 39%  
o	Acq Cost % rising from 12% to 13%  
- Therefore, the jump in UW margin is not operationally credible without considering reserve release.  
Underwriting quality conclusion  
- **FY26** booked profitability is not high-quality profitability  
- It is reserve-assisted / reserve-release-driven  
- Underwriters should not use **FY26** reported profit alone to expand appetite  
Adequacy of premium versus claims  
At the underlying level, premium adequacy worsened.  
- **NEP** increased by only 55 (+4.6%)  
- **NIC** Before **IBNR** increased by **333** (+57.6%)  
- That means claims rose far faster than earned premium.  
- The result is Incurred LR worsening from 49% to 73% (+24 pts).  
Business implication  
- The book was not being priced adequately enough to absorb the underlying claims deterioration.  
- Whatever made the booked result look better was not premium adequacy; it was the reserve swing.  
Reserve dependence  
This portfolio is clearly reserve-dependent in **FY26**.  
Evidence:  
- **IBNR**: +**621** to -**669** (-1,**290**)  
- **NIC** After **IBNR**: 1,**199** to **241** (-**958**)  
- Financial LR: **101**% to 19%  
- **COR**: 84% to 26%  
- UW Result: **182** to **922**  
Interpretation  
The portfolioâ€™s reported recovery depends very heavily on reserve movement. That is not inherently wrong, but it means:  
- current year booked performance may not be reproducible  
- branch / segment appetite decisions should be based more on **NIC** Before **IBNR** / Incurred LR than on final booked **COR**  
Segments / locations causing underwriting stress  
1. Delhi - Narain Manzil  
This is the largest genuine underwriting stress point.  
- **GWP**: 1,**428** to 1,**485** (+57, +4.0%)  
- **NEP**: **342** to **349** (+7, +2.0%)  
- **NIC** Before **IBNR**: **261** to **357** (+96, +36.8%)  
- **IBNR**: -**209** to +**180** (+**389**)  
- **NIC** After **IBNR**: 52 to **537** (+**485**, +**932**.7%)  
- Financial LR: 15% to **154**% (+**139** pts)  
- Incurred LR: 76% to **102**% (+26 pts)  
- UW Result: +**323** to -**208** (-**531**)  
- **COR**: 5% to **159**% (+**154** pts)  
Underwriting interpretation  
- Premium growth was modest, but underlying claims and reserves both worsened.  
- This is not a reserve-only issue; the Incurred LR at **102**% shows real underwriting failure.  
- Delhi needs immediate underwriting correction.  
________________________________________  
2. Pune - Metro House  
Pune is the sharpest ratio deterioration in the portfolio.  
- **GWP**: **219** to **203** (-16, -7.3%)  
- **NEP**: 45 to 56 (+11, +24.4%)  
- **NIC** Before **IBNR**: -1 to **195** (+**196**)  
- **IBNR**: -6 to +14 (+20)  
- **NIC** After **IBNR**: -6 to **210** (+**216**)  
- Financial LR: -15% to **372**% (+**387** pts)  
- Incurred LR: -1% to **346**% (+**347** pts)  
- UW Result: +57 to -**153** (-**210**)  
- **COR**: -29% to **371**% (+**400** pts)  
Underwriting interpretation  
- Severe claims emergence and reserve strengthening.  
- This branch moved from benign / favorable development to acute stress.  
- It should be treated as urgent corrective priority despite smaller size.  
________________________________________  
3. Ahmedabad - **BBC**  
Ahmedabad shows a very large booked loss emergence, mainly reserve-led.  
- **GWP**: **604** to **661** (+57, +9.4%)  
- **NEP**: **137** to **166** (+29, +21.2%)  
- **NIC** Before **IBNR**: 65 to 86 (+21, +32.3%)  
- **IBNR**: -**446** to +**377** (+**823**)  
- **NIC** After **IBNR**: -**381** to +**463** (+**844**)  
- Financial LR: -**278**% to **278**% (+**556** pts)  
- Incurred LR: 47% to 52% (+5 pts)  
- UW Result: +**507** to -**340** (-**847**)  
- **COR**: -**270**% to **307**% (+**577** pts)  
Underwriting interpretation  
- Underlying claims worsened only modestly (**ILR** +5 pts), but booked performance collapsed because reserves moved sharply adverse.  
- This is a classic case of reserve dependency masking true branch profitability.  
________________________________________  
4. Retail vertical  
Retail is the largest poor-quality growth segment.  
- **GWP**: **590** to **750** (+**160**, +27.1%)  
- **NEP**: **144** to **175** (+31, +21.5%)  
- **NIC** Before **IBNR**: 54 to **131** (+77, +**142**.6%)  
- **IBNR**: -34 to -3 (+31), i.e. much less reserve release  
- **NIC** After **IBNR**: 20 to **128** (+**108**, +**540**%)  
- Financial LR: 14% to 73% (+59 pts)  
- Incurred LR: 38% to 75% (+37 pts)  
- UW Result: +89 to -56 (-**145**)  
- **COR**: 40% to **133**% (+93 pts)  
Underwriting interpretation  
- Retail grew strongly but with meaningfully worse claims and weaker net economics.  
- This is not acceptable quality growth.  
________________________________________  
5. Emerging vertical  
Emerging is still small, but quality is poor.  
- **GWP**: 26 to 47 (+21, +80.8%)  
- **NEP**: 6 to 11 (+5, +83.3%)  
- **NIC** After **IBNR**: 0 to 6  
- Incurred LR: 10% to 53% (+43 pts)  
- Acq Cost %: 25% to 29% (+4 pts)  
- Commission Ratio: 17% to 43% (+26 pts)  
- UW Result: 0 to -5  
- **COR**: **109**% to **143**% (+34 pts)  
Underwriting interpretation  
- High growth, very small scale, weak economics, negative underwriting.  
- This is a do not expand segment in current form.  
Segments / locations showing strong underwriting quality  
1. Hyderabad - Punjagutta  
This is the best genuine underwriting improvement.  
- **GWP**: **351** to **318** (-33, -9.4%)  
- **NEP**: 75 to 86 (+11, +14.7%)  
- **NIC** Before **IBNR**: 95 to 31 (-64, -67.4%)  
- **IBNR**: -19 to +13 (+32)  
- **NIC** After **IBNR**: 76 to 44 (-32, -42.1%)  
- Financial LR: **101**% to 51% (-50 pts)  
- Incurred LR: **126**% to 36% (-90 pts)  
- UW Result: -9 to +23 (+32)  
- **COR**: **112**% to 77% (-35 pts)  
Underwriting interpretation  
- This looks like a real improvement, not just a reserve artifact.  
- Claims improved strongly before **IBNR**, and the branch moved from loss to profit.  
________________________________________  
2. Chennai - Chotabhai Centre  
Chennai delivered healthy growth, but quality softened.  
- **GWP**: **362** to **490** (+**128**, +35.4%)  
- **NEP**: 67 to **102** (+35, +52.2%)  
- **NIC** Before **IBNR**: 7 to 39 (+32, +**457**%)  
- **NIC** After **IBNR**: 2 to 40 (+38, +1,**900**%)  
- Incurred LR: 10% to 38% (+28 pts)  
- UW Result: 69 to 24 (-45, -65.2%)  
- **COR**: -3% to 73% (+76 pts)  
Underwriting interpretation  
- Still profitable and still acceptable on reported **COR**, but quality is weaker than **FY25**.  
- This is good growth, but not as clean as it first appears.  
________________________________________  
3. **SME** Broking  
Best vertical for sustainable underwriting quality.  
- **GWP**: **218** to **232** (+14, +6.4%)  
- **NEP**: 48 to 73 (+25, +52.1%)  
- **NIC** Before **IBNR**: 18 to 23 (+5, +27.8%)  
- **NIC** After **IBNR**: 13 to 25 (+12, +92.3%)  
- Financial LR: 27% to 35% (+8 pts)  
- Incurred LR: 36% to 32% (-4 pts)  
- Acq Cost %: 24% to 22% (-2 pts)  
- Expense Ratio: 28% to 25% (-3 pts)  
- UW Result: 24 to 25 (+1)  
- **COR**: 48% to 67% (+19 pts)  
Underwriting interpretation  
- Not perfect, but this is the best-balanced vertical:   
o	claims manageable  
o	underwriting result positive  
o	acquisition and expense improved  
- Better quality than Retail and Emerging by a wide margin.  
Sustainable vs volatile business  
Sustainable / higher-quality  
- Hyderabad  
- **SME** Broking  
- Chennai (positive but weaker than last year)  
Volatile / reserve-distorted  
- Mumbai  
- Ahmedabad  
- Bangalore  
- Kolkata  
These locations show strong distortion between underlying claims and booked results because reserve movement is large.  
High-risk / deteriorating  
- Delhi  
- Pune  
- Retail  
- Emerging  
Appetite expansion opportunities  
Scale aggressively  
- Hyderabad  
- **SME** Broking  
Grow selectively  
- Chennai  
- Corporate only in better-performing risk cohorts, not broad-brush  
Hold / monitor  
- Kolkata  
- Indore  
- Bangalore  
- Fire Segment: **MID** vs Mid + **SME** + Retail  
Correct urgently  
- Delhi  
- Pune  
- Retail  
De-risk / tighten  
- Emerging  
- Ahmedabad (until reserve adequacy is understood)  
- Mumbai (not because of current reported profit, but because quality is clearly reserve-dependent)  
Pricing / deductible / wording / referral / reinsurance implications  
- Pricing: Delhi, Pune, Retail, and parts of Corporate need repricing. Claims have risen much faster than earned premium in these pockets.  
- Deductibles: Tighten deductibles / excess structures where high-frequency or accumulation-driven claims are surfacing.  
- Wording: Review policy wordings for broad extensions, debris removal, BI attachments, escalation clauses, and claims trigger interpretation.  
- Referral: Make all large risks from deteriorating branches referral-mandatory, especially:   
o	Delhi  
o	Pune  
o	Ahmedabad  
o	weak Retail cohorts  
- Reinsurance: Reassess ceding strategy and RI commission economics. Ceding reduced marginally, but RI commission fell 10.7%. The business may be carrying weaker net economics without getting proportionate risk relief.  
________________________________________  
## RM / Sales / Distribution Perspective  
Where growth is strong and healthy  
Chennai  
- **GWP** grew from **362** to **490** (+**128**, +35.4%)  
- **NEP** grew from 67 to **102** (+35, +52.2%)  
- UW Result remained positive at 24  
- **COR** is still manageable at 73%  
- RM interpretation: growth is commercially strong and still profitable, though quality has weakened. This is growth worth retaining, but not at any price.  
**SME** Broking  
- **GWP** grew from **218** to **232** (+14, +6.4%)  
- **NEP** grew from 48 to 73 (+25, +52.1%)  
- UW Result stayed positive at 25  
- Incurred LR improved from 36% to 32%  
- RM interpretation: this is the most attractive RM-led growth pocket. Expansion is justified.  
Indore (small scale only)  
- **GWP** grew from 29 to 64 (+35, +**120**.7%)  
- **NEP** grew from 10 to 12 (+2, +20.0%)  
- UW Result stayed positive at 7  
- **COR** is 37%  
- RM interpretation: good direction, but scale is tiny. This is not a strategic growth engine yet.  
Where growth is weak or low-quality  
Delhi  
- **GWP** +57 (+4.0%), but UW Result -**531**  
- **ILR** 76% to **102**%  
- **COR** 5% to **159**%  
- RM implication: top-line growth is unacceptable when it destroys underwriting profitability.  
Retail  
- **GWP** +**160** (+27.1%)  
- **NEP** +31 (+21.5%)  
- UW +89 to -56  
- **COR** 40% to **133**%  
- RM implication: Retail teams are adding volume, but the portfolio cannot currently absorb it profitably.  
Emerging  
- **GWP** +80.8%  
- UW 0 to -5  
- Acq Cost % 25% to 29%  
- Commission Ratio 17% to 43%  
- RM implication: this is expensive, low-scale, poor-quality growth.  
Where RMs should focus more  
- Hyderabad: even with lower **GWP**, underwriting improved materially and branch economics are healthier.  
- Chennai: scalable growth still exists, but it needs underwriting guardrails.  
- **SME** Broking: best quality growth pocket.  
- Selective Corporate sub-segments: only where claims and expense discipline support expansion.  
Where RMs should avoid pushing volume  
- Delhi  
- Retail  
- Emerging  
- Pune  
- Ahmedabad, until reserve volatility is fully understood  
Which segments / regions look attractive  
Attractive  
- Hyderabad  
- **SME** Broking  
- Chennai (with discipline)  
- Selective Corporate niches  
Unattractive / stressed  
- Delhi  
- Retail  
- Emerging  
- Pune  
- Reserve-distorted Mumbai, where the reported profit should not mislead RM strategy  
Whether acquisition cost is justified  
At portfolio level, not fully.  
- Acq Cost Mil increased **824** to **847** (+23, +2.8%)  
- Acq Cost % increased 12% to 13%  
- At the same time:   
o	Incurred LR worsened by 24 pts  
o	Expense Ratio worsened by 7 pts  
o	RI Commission fell by **148**  
- This means the portfolio is paying slightly more to acquire business, but the real underlying economics are weaker.  
Justified  
- **SME** Broking  
- Chennai (conditionally)  
- Hyderabad if growth quality can be rebuilt  
Not justified  
- Retail  
- Emerging  
- Delhi  
- Pune  
- Ahmedabad  
Whether customer mix looks favorable or unfavorable  
- Corporate remains the dominant mix at 84.4% of **GWP**, but quality is deteriorating.  
- Retail is becoming unfavorable: growth is strong, but claims and **COR** are materially worse.  
- **SME** Broking mix looks favorable.  
- Emerging mix currently looks weak because cost and claims rose faster than scale.  
Which areas are suitable for expansion  
- **SME** Broking  
- Hyderabad  
- Chennai with stronger underwriting controls  
Where sales strategy should shift from volume to quality  
- Retail  
- Delhi  
- Emerging  
- Pune  
- Ahmedabad  
Where cross-sell / up-sell / renewal / retention should be emphasized  
- Hyderabad: defend and deepen quality accounts  
- **SME** Broking: cross-sell is justified  
- Chennai: maintain growth through renewal and better-risk upsell rather than aggressive new business  
- Corporate: use retention strategy selectively on good accounts; do not broadly defend underpriced or deteriorating risks  
________________________________________  
## Geography / Segment / Channel / Product Deep Dive  
- Geography / Location Deep Dive  
1. **AHMEDABAD** - **BBC**  
- One-line summary: Good top-line growth, but booked profitability collapsed due to major adverse reserve movement.  
- Top positive: **GWP** **604** to **661** (+57, +9.4%), **NEP** **137** to **166** (+29, +21.2%)  
- Top concern: UW **507** to -**340** (-**847**) and **COR** -**270**% to **307**% (+**577** pts)  
- Underwriting interpretation: Underlying claims worsened modestly (**ILR** 47% to 52%), but reserve strengthening (**IBNR** -**446** to +**377**) destroyed profitability.  
- RM interpretation: Premium growth here is not commercially usable until reserve adequacy and pricing are revalidated.  
- Exact reason using numbers: **NIC** Before **IBNR** 65 to 86 (+21); **NIC** After **IBNR** -**381** to **463** (+**844**) due to **IBNR** swing of +**823**.  
- Recommended action: De-risk / tighten until reserve issue is understood.  
2. **BANGALORE** - **RICHMOND** **ROAD**  
- One-line summary: Small branch with flat premium, better underlying claims, but booked profitability turned negative due to reserve movement.  
- Top positive: Expense Ratio improved 43% to 24% (-19 pts) and Acq Cost % improved 18% to 16% (-2 pts)  
- Top concern: UW **144** to -3 (-**147**) and **COR** -**299**% to **106**% (+**405** pts)  
- Underwriting interpretation: Possible interpretation based on available data: underlying claims improved (**NIC** Before **IBNR** 3 to -20; **ILR** 9% to -58%), but reserve strengthening (**IBNR** -92 to +68) worsened booked result.  
- RM interpretation: Avoid reading **FY25** super-profitability as repeatable; branch is too reserve-sensitive.  
- Exact reason using numbers: **NIC** After **IBNR** -88 to 47 (+**135**) despite lower **GWP** and **NEP**.  
- Recommended action: Hold / monitor  
3. **CHENNAI**-**CHOTABHAI** **CENTRE**  
- One-line summary: Strong growth with still-positive underwriting, but claims and costs worsened materially.  
- Top positive: **GWP** **362** to **490** (+**128**, +35.4%), **NEP** 67 to **102** (+35, +52.2%)  
- Top concern: UW 69 to 24 (-45, -65.2%) and **COR** -3% to 73% (+76 pts)  
- Underwriting interpretation: Still profitable, but underwriting quality has weakened notably.  
- RM interpretation: Good-quality growth versus the broader portfolio, but should now shift to rate and selection discipline.  
- Exact reason using numbers: **NIC** Before **IBNR** 7 to 39 (+32), **ILR** 10% to 38% (+28 pts), Expense Ratio 30% to 37% (+7 pts).  
- Recommended action: Grow selectively  
4. **DELHI** - **NARAIN** **MANZIL**  
- One-line summary: Large branch with modest growth but severe underwriting deterioration.  
- Top positive: **GWP** still grew 1,**428** to 1,**485** (+57, +4.0%)  
- Top concern: UW +**323** to -**208** (-**531**) and **COR** 5% to **159**% (+**154** pts)  
- Underwriting interpretation: Claims stress is real and not merely reserve-related; this is the biggest substantive problem branch.  
- RM interpretation: Stop chasing top-line here until pricing, sector mix, and underwriting controls are fixed.  
- Exact reason using numbers: **ILR** 76% to **102**% (+26 pts), **NIC** After **IBNR** 52 to **537** (+**485**), Acq Cost % 15% to 17%, Comm Ratio -37% to -21%  
- Recommended action: Correct urgently  
5. **GEO** - **INDORE**  
- One-line summary: Small branch with strong growth and acceptable profitability, but scale is very low.  
- Top positive: **GWP** 29 to 64 (+35, +**120**.7%), **COR** -78% to 37%  
- Top concern: Too small to matter strategically; **NEP** only 12  
- Underwriting interpretation: Underlying claims improved (**ILR** 13% to 3%), and underwriting remained positive.  
- RM interpretation: Encouraging, but not yet a major growth engine.  
- Exact reason using numbers: UW 19 to 7 (-12) mainly because reserve benefit weakened, not because claims blew up.  
- Recommended action: Hold / monitor / selective growth  
6. **HYDERABAD** - **PUNJAGUTTA**  
- One-line summary: Best genuine underwriting improvement in the visible branch set.  
- Top positive: **ILR** **126**% to 36% (-90 pts) and UW -9 to +23 (+32)  
- Top concern: **GWP** declined **351** to **318** (-33, -9.4%)  
- Underwriting interpretation: Real claims improvement with positive underwriting turn.  
- RM interpretation: This is the best branch to defend and selectively scale.  
- Exact reason using numbers: **NIC** Before **IBNR** 95 to 31 (-64), **NIC** After **IBNR** 76 to 44 (-32), **COR** **112**% to 77%  
- Recommended action: Scale aggressively  
7. **KOLKATA**-JK **MILLENIUM**  
- One-line summary: Moderate growth, but quality deteriorated sharply.  
- Top positive: **GWP** **249** to **298** (+49, +19.7%)  
- Top concern: UW **153** to 7 (-**146**) and **COR** -**120**% to 92% (+**212** pts)  
- Underwriting interpretation: Both claims and reserving worsened.  
- RM interpretation: Growth is not translating into attractive profitability.  
- Exact reason using numbers: **ILR** -9% to 33% (+42 pts), Expense Ratio 28% to 52% (+24 pts), Acq Cost % 16% to 19%  
- Recommended action: Hold / monitor  
8. **MUMBAI**  
- One-line summary: Largest branch and biggest reported profit swing, but improvement is overwhelmingly reserve-release-driven.  
- Top positive: UW -1,**083** to +1,**565** (+2,**648**) and **COR** **368**% to -**333**% (-**701** pts)  
- Top concern: Underlying claims worsened and the booked result is not sustainable.  
- Underwriting interpretation: This is not a clean turnaround. It is dominated by **IBNR** +1,**473** to -1,**346** (-2,**819**).  
- RM interpretation: Do not use Mumbaiâ€™s **FY26** reported profit to justify aggressive top-line push.  
- Exact reason using numbers: **GWP** 3,**247** to 2,**945** (-**302**, -9.3%), **NEP** **405** to **363** (-42, -10.4%), **ILR** 38% to 55% (+17 pts), Expense Ratio 34% to 56% (+22 pts).  
- Recommended action: De-risk / tighten / re-understand reserve position first  
9. **PUNE**-**METRO** **HOUSE**  
- One-line summary: Small branch with catastrophic claims deterioration and severe underwriting loss.  
- Top positive: Almost none in **FY26**; only slight reduction in acquisition ratio 20% to 15%  
- Top concern: **ILR** -1% to **346**% (+**347** pts), UW 57 to -**153** (-**210**), **COR** -29% to **371**% (+**400** pts)  
- Underwriting interpretation: Acute deterioration requiring immediate intervention.  
- RM interpretation: Stop chasing any volume until the claims drivers are diagnosed.  
- Exact reason using numbers: **NIC** Before **IBNR** -1 to **195** (+**196**) and **NIC** After **IBNR** -6 to **210** (+**216**)  
- Recommended action: Correct urgently  
________________________________________  
- Vertical / Segment Deep Dive  
10. Corporate  
- One-line summary: Core book still profitable, but materially weaker.  
- Top positive: Still produced UW **234** at scale  
- Top concern: UW **886** to **234** (-**652**, -73.6%), **COR** 10% to 76% (+66 pts)  
- Underwriting interpretation: Underlying claims worsened significantly, and the segment remains heavily dependent on reinsurance structure.  
- RM interpretation: Do not push broad growth; segment needs account-quality discipline.  
- Exact reason using numbers: **GWP** 5,**798** to 5,**575** (-**223**, -3.9%), **NEP** **992** to **985** (-7), **NIC** Before **IBNR** **495** to **750** (+**255**), **ILR** 50% to 76% (+26 pts), Expense Ratio 30% to 39%  
- Recommended action: Grow selectively / hold in weaker pockets  
11. Emerging  
- One-line summary: High growth, very poor economics, negative underwriting.  
- Top positive: **GWP** 26 to 47 (+21, +80.8%)  
- Top concern: UW 0 to -5, **COR** **109**% to **143**%  
- Underwriting interpretation: Underpriced / high-cost / low-scale book.  
- RM interpretation: Growth here should not be rewarded in current form.  
- Exact reason using numbers: **ILR** 10% to 53% (+43 pts), Acq Cost % 25% to 29%, Commission Ratio 17% to 43%  
- Recommended action: De-risk / tighten  
12. Retail  
- One-line summary: Strong premium growth, but decisively poor-quality business.  
- Top positive: **GWP** **590** to **750** (+**160**, +27.1%)  
- Top concern: UW 89 to -56 (-**145**), **COR** 40% to **133**% (+93 pts)  
- Underwriting interpretation: The segment grew in the wrong directionâ€”more premium, much worse loss and cost quality.  
- RM interpretation: Shift immediately from volume to profitability discipline.  
- Exact reason using numbers: **NIC** Before **IBNR** 54 to **131** (+77), **NIC** After **IBNR** 20 to **128** (+**108**), **ILR** 38% to 75% (+37 pts), Commission Ratio -21% to 15% (+36 pts)  
- Recommended action: Correct urgently  
13. **SME** Broking  
- One-line summary: Best visible segment on genuine underwriting sustainability.  
- Top positive: **ILR** 36% to 32% (-4 pts) and UW 24 to 25  
- Top concern: **COR** 48% to 67% (+19 pts) because financial loss ratio and commission ratio worsened  
- Underwriting interpretation: Best balance of claims, cost, and outcome.  
- RM interpretation: Best segment for targeted expansion.  
- Exact reason using numbers: **NEP** 48 to 73 (+25), Acq Cost % 24% to 22%, Expense Ratio 28% to 25%  
- Recommended action: Scale aggressively  
14. **FIRE** **SEGMENT**: **MID** vs Mid + **SME** + Retail  
- One-line summary: Flat **GWP**, weaker profitability, close to breakeven underwriting.  
- Top positive: Acq Cost % 24% to 23%  
- Top concern: UW 24 to 1 (-23) and **COR** 49% to 96% (+47 pts)  
- Underwriting interpretation: Deteriorating claims quality and weaker net economics.  
- RM interpretation: Defend selectively, not an obvious expansion area.  
- Exact reason using numbers: **ILR** 36% to 46% (+10 pts), Financial LR 27% to 54% (+27 pts), Commission Ratio -6% to 15% (+21 pts)  
- Recommended action: Hold / monitor

## Key Risks and Red Flags  
- Margin compression beneath reported profit  
o	Underlying Incurred LR worsened from 49% to 73% (+24 pts)  
o	Expense Ratio worsened from 32% to 39% (+7 pts)  
- Reserve dependency  
o	**IBNR** swung by -1,**290**  
o	Reported UW and **COR** are heavily reserve-driven  
- Adverse claims emergence  
o	**NIC** Before **IBNR** increased by **333** (+57.6%)  
- Weak reinsurance economics  
o	RI Comm fell by **148** (-10.7%)  
o	Commission Ratio worsened by 16 pts  
- Poor acquisition efficiency  
o	Acq Cost % increased 12% to 13%  
o	Acquisition spend rose despite flat **GWP**  
- Unstable profitability  
o	Ahmedabad, Mumbai, Bangalore, Kolkata, and Pune all show large reserve-linked swings  
- Unsustainable growth patterns  
o	Retail and Emerging grew, but profitability deteriorated sharply  
o	Delhi grew while turning deeply loss-making  
- High concentration risk  
o	Corporate = 84.4% of **FY26** **GWP**  
o	Mumbai = 44.6% of **FY26** **GWP**  
o	A single location / segment swing can distort the whole portfolio  
- Data inconsistency / reporting complexity  
o	**NEP** across locations sums to 1,**243** vs total 1,**244**  
o	**FY25** UW across locations sums to **180** vs total **182**  
o	Metrics need careful governance before strategic overreaction

## Recommended Actions  
Underwriting actions  
## Rebase portfolio review on Incurred LR (pre-IBNR), not only booked COR  
## Immediate corrective underwriting action in Delhi and Pune   
o	reprice  
o	tighten wordings  
o	increase deductibles  
o	account-level referral  
## Reserve adequacy review in Ahmedabad and Mumbai   
o	understand why reserve positions swung so sharply  
## Retail portfolio repair   
o	tighten new business appetite  
o	reprice renewal business  
o	eliminate weakest cohorts  
## Protect and scale Hyderabad / SME Broking   
o	keep pricing discipline intact  
RM / distribution actions  
## Stop rewarding top-line growth where UW is negative   
o	Delhi  
o	Retail  
o	Emerging  
o	Pune  
## Prioritize quality-led growth   
o	Chennai  
o	**SME** Broking  
o	Hyderabad  
## Shift RM scorecards from premium to profitability   
o	add **COR** / **ILR** / UW Result gates  
## Renewal strategy   
o	defend profitable accounts  
o	do not over-defend deteriorating risks in Corporate / Retail  
## Broker / channel review   
o	especially where acquisition cost and commission economics deteriorated without corresponding claims quality  
Portfolio management actions  
## Separate reserve-driven profit from operating underwriting profit in review packs  
## Set branch- and segment-level guardrails   
o	max **ILR**  
o	max **COR**  
o	max Acq %  
o	referral threshold  
## Reduce dependence on reserve releases for profitability  
## Revisit reinsurance structure   
o	especially given lower RI commission support  
## Rebalance mix   
o	away from stressed Retail / Emerging  
o	toward better-quality **SME** Broking / selected Hyderabad / Chennai-type business  
Data / dashboard actions  
## Add a dedicated split between:   
o	**NIC** Before **IBNR**  
o	**IBNR** movement  
o	**NIC** After **IBNR**  
## Show branch-wise pre-IBNR vs post-IBNR profitability  
## Reconcile location and segment totals to portfolio totals  
## Add account-level / sector-level claims cohort view  
## Add renewal vs new business profitability view  
## Add RI economics view:   
o	ceding ratio  
o	RI commission  
o	net retention profitability  
________________________________________  
## Final Conclusion  
Is the portfolio improving or deteriorating?  
- Reported performance is improving sharply  
- Underlying underwriting quality is deteriorating  
Is growth profitable or poor quality?  
- Mostly poor quality where growth exists, especially in:   
o	Retail  
o	Emerging  
o	Delhi  
- The exceptions are:   
o	Chennai  
o	**SME** Broking  
o	selective Indore  
o	and operational recovery in Hyderabad  
Which areas should be scaled?  
- **HYDERABAD** - **PUNJAGUTTA**  
- **SME** Broking  
- **CHENNAI**-**CHOTABHAI** **CENTRE** (selectively and with tighter underwriting)  
Which areas should be corrected?  
- **DELHI** - **NARAIN** **MANZIL**  
- **PUNE**-**METRO** **HOUSE**  
- Retail  
- Corporate pockets with worsening **ILR**  
Which areas should be de-risked?  
- **MUMBAI** (because reported profit is not reliable as underlying quality metric)  
- **AHMEDABAD** - **BBC**  
- Emerging  
- any branch / segment where reserve swing is masking poor core claims experience

## Trend chart   
o	Retention, **ILR**, **FLR**, Acq %, Expense Ratio, **COR**  
## Heatmap   
o	branch / segment by **ILR**, **COR**, UW Result, reserve movement  
Most useful filters / slicers if detailed data were available  
- Period (month / quarter / **YTD**)  
- Branch / geography / zone  
- Vertical / segment  
- Corporate vs Retail vs **SME**  
- New business vs renewal  
- Broker / RM / channel / source  
- Occupancy / industry / sum insured band  
- Treaty type / RI structure  
- Claim status / claim year / underwriting year  
- Reserve movement type (case reserve / **IBNR** / release / strengthening)  

Top 5:  
## Key portfolio message  
- Top-line was flat, but reported profitability improved sharply.  
- **GWP** declined marginally from 6,**632** to 6,**603** (-29, -0.4%), while UW Result increased from **182** to **922** (+**740**, +**406**.6%) and **COR** improved from 84% to 26% (-58 pts).  
- However, this is not a clean underwriting improvement.  
- Underlying claims worsened materially: **NIC** Before **IBNR** rose from **578** to **911** (+**333**, +57.6%) and Incurred LR increased from 49% to 73% (+24 pts).  
- The reported turnaround was driven primarily by reserve movement, with **IBNR** swinging from +**621** to -**669** (-1,**290**), pulling **NIC** After **IBNR** down from 1,**199** to **241** (-**958**, -79.9%).  
- Leadership message: reported profit is up, but core underwriting quality is weaker and reserve-dependent.  
________________________________________  
## Underwriting message  
- Do not read **FY26** as a true underwriting recovery.  
- Core underwriting quality deteriorated despite the reported profit uplift:   
o	Incurred LR: 49% to 73% (+24 pts)  
o	Expense Ratio: 32% to 39% (+7 pts)  
o	Acq Cost %: 12% to 13% (+1 pt)  
- The biggest underwriting stress points are:   
o	Delhi: UW +**323** to -**208** (-**531**); **COR** 5% to **159**% (+**154** pts); **ILR** 76% to **102**% (+26 pts)  
o	Pune: UW +57 to -**153** (-**210**); **COR** -29% to **371**% (+**400** pts); **ILR** -1% to **346**% (+**347** pts)  
o	Retail: UW +89 to -56 (-**145**); **COR** 40% to **133**% (+93 pts); **ILR** 38% to 75% (+37 pts)  
- The strongest genuine underwriting improvement is Hyderabad:   
o	UW -9 to +23 (+32)  
o	**ILR** **126**% to 36% (-90 pts)  
o	**COR** **112**% to 77% (-35 pts)  
- Mumbaiâ€™s reported turnaround is reserve-led, not underwriting-led:   
o	UW -1,**083** to +1,**565** (+2,**648**)  
o	but **ILR** worsened from 38% to 55% (+17 pts)  
o	and **IBNR** moved from +1,**473** to -1,**346** (-2,**819**)  
________________________________________  
## RM message  
- Growth quality is mixed and needs tighter discipline.  
- Healthy / usable growth is concentrated in:   
o	Chennai: **GWP** **362** to **490** (+**128**, +35.4%), UW still positive at 24  
o	**SME** Broking: **GWP** **218** to **232** (+14, +6.4%), UW 24 to 25 (+1), **ILR** 36% to 32% (-4 pts)  
o	Hyderabad: lower **GWP**, but much better underwriting quality  
- Poor-quality growth is concentrated in:   
o	Delhi: premium growth with severe loss-making outcome  
o	Retail: strong growth but underwriting turned negative  
o	Emerging: **GWP** +80.8%, but UW 0 to -5 and **COR** **109**% to **143**%  
- Sales cost efficiency weakened:   
o	Acquisition Cost rose from **824** to **847** (+23, +2.8%)  
o	Acq Cost % rose from 12% to 13%  
o	RI Commission fell from 1,**383** to 1,**235** (-**148**, -10.7%)  
- RM message to leadership: stop rewarding volume without underwriting quality. Focus should shift from premium growth to profitable retention, better mix, and risk selection.  
________________________________________  
## Top 5 strengths  
## Reported portfolio profitability improved sharply  
o	UW Result: **182** to **922** (+**740**)  
o	**COR**: 84% to 26% (-58 pts)  
## Retention improved slightly  
o	Retention ratio: 17.5% to 18.1% (+0.6 pts)  
## Hyderabad delivered the best genuine underwriting recovery  
o	UW: -9 to +23  
o	**ILR**: **126**% to 36%  
o	**COR**: **112**% to 77%  
## Chennai delivered scalable growth while staying profitable  
o	**GWP**: +**128** (+35.4%)  
o	**NEP**: +35 (+52.2%)  
o	UW remained positive at 24  
## SME Broking is the cleanest segment  
o	UW: 24 to 25  
o	**ILR**: 36% to 32%  
o	Acq Cost %: 24% to 22%  
o	Expense Ratio: 28% to 25%  
________________________________________  
## Top 5 concerns  
## Reported improvement is heavily reserve-dependent  
o	**IBNR**: +**621** to -**669** (-1,**290**)  
o	This is the main reason booked claims and **COR** improved  
## Underlying claims worsened materially  
o	**NIC** Before **IBNR**: **578** to **911** (+**333**, +57.6%)  
o	Incurred LR: 49% to 73% (+24 pts)  
## Delhi is a major value-destructive branch  
o	UW: +**323** to -**208**  
o	**COR**: 5% to **159**%  
o	**ILR**: 76% to **102**%  
## Retail growth is poor-quality growth  
o	**GWP**: +**160** (+27.1%)  
o	UW: +89 to -56  
o	**COR**: 40% to **133**%  
## Mumbaiâ€™s apparent turnaround is misleading  
o	UW: -1,**083** to +1,**565**  
o	but **ILR** worsened 38% to 55%  
o	and the result is dominated by **IBNR** release / reversal  
________________________________________  
## Immediate actions  
- Rebase portfolio review on pre-**IBNR** performance  
o	Use **NIC** Before **IBNR** and Incurred LR as primary underwriting quality metrics  
- Correct Delhi immediately  
o	Reprice  
o	tighten risk selection  
o	apply referral controls  
o	review large accounts and sector mix  
- Intervene urgently in Pune and Retail  
o	Stop volume-chasing  
o	diagnose claims drivers  
o	repair pricing and renewal terms  
- Do not over-read Mumbai profitability  
o	conduct reserve validation before using Mumbai as a growth template  
- Scale the cleaner pockets  
o	Hyderabad  
o	**SME** Broking  
o	Chennai (selectively, with tighter underwriting guardrails)  
- Reset RM scorecards  
o	reward UW Result, **ILR**, **COR**, and retention quality, not **GWP** alone  
- Review reinsurance economics  
o	falling RI Commission and very high ceding require a sharper net profitability lens  
________________________________________

## Executive Summary  
- Bharat Sookshma has moved from a marginal underwriting profit to a meaningful underwriting loss. UW result deteriorated from â‚ą37m profit in **YTD**-Mar-25 to â‚ą194m loss in **YTD**-Mar-26 (-â‚ą231m deterioration), while **COR** worsened from 84% to **162**% (+78 pts).  
- The headline top-line decline is modest, but the profitability collapse is driven by reserve support disappearing and expenses inflating. **GWP** declined from â‚ą1,770m to â‚ą1,649m (-â‚ą121m, -6.8%), yet **NEP** increased from â‚ą320m to â‚ą352m (+â‚ą32m, +10.0%). Despite better earned premium, **NIC** After **IBNR** rose from â‚ą74m to â‚ą202m (+â‚ą128m, +**173**.0%) and expense increased from â‚ą307m to â‚ą373m (+â‚ą66m, +21.5%).  
- The biggest portfolio-quality issue is not gross claims emergence alone; it is loss of reserve benefit. **NIC** Before **IBNR** actually improved from â‚ą240m to â‚ą211m (-â‚ą29m, -12.1%), but **IBNR** shifted from a release of â‚ą166m to a release of only â‚ą10m, i.e. +â‚ą156m adverse swing, causing net incurred claims to jump.  
- The portfolio remains extremely heavily ceded, but retention is broadly flat/slightly better. Retention (**NWP**/**GWP**) improved marginally from 19.4% to 19.9% (+0.5 pts), while ceding reduced from 80.6% to 80.1% (-0.5 pts). So the deterioration is not primarily a retention failure.  
- **NEP** quality improved, but economics still failed because cost and reserve support turned adverse. **NEP**/**GWP** rose from 18.1% to 21.4% (+3.3 pts), helped by PY **URR** increasing from â‚ą199m to â‚ą222m (+â‚ą23m) and CY release increasing from â‚ą230m to â‚ą249m (+â‚ą19m).  
- The book is structurally expense-heavy. Expense ratio increased from 90% to **114**% (+24 pts). Even with claims under control, this portfolio would struggle to make money unless expense intensity materially reduces.  
- Retail is the core problem segment by scale. Retail **GWP** reduced from â‚ą1,574m to â‚ą1,485m (-â‚ą89m, -5.7%), but expense increased from â‚ą272m to â‚ą346m (+â‚ą74m, +27.2%), Acq Cost % worsened from 16% to 17% (+1 pt), and UW loss deepened from â‚ą91m to â‚ą162m (-â‚ą71m) despite **NIC** dropping from â‚ą174m to â‚ą143m (-â‚ą31m, -17.8%).  
- Delhi and Kolkata are the biggest scale deterioration pockets from an underwriting perspective.   
o	Delhi: **UWR** â‚ą58m to â‚ą(78)m (-â‚ą136m), **NIC** â‚ą(34)m to â‚ą85m (+â‚ą119m), **COR** 27% to **194**% (+**167** pts).  
o	Kolkata: **UWR** â‚ą13m to â‚ą(46)m (-â‚ą59m), **NIC** â‚ą(2)m to â‚ą45m (+â‚ą47m), **COR** 50% to **266**% (+**216** pts).  
- Mumbai is the only large geography growing in both **GWP** and **NEP**, but it is still poor-quality growth. **GWP** increased from â‚ą540m to â‚ą595m (+â‚ą55m, +10.2%), **NEP** increased from â‚ą85m to â‚ą110m (+â‚ą25m, +29.4%), and **NIC** improved from â‚ą57m to â‚ą46m (-â‚ą11m, -19.3%); however, expense rose from â‚ą98m to â‚ą134m (+â‚ą36m, +36.7%), so **UWR** worsened from â‚ą(14)m to â‚ą(28)m (-â‚ą14m) and **COR** worsened from **107**% to **125**% (+18 pts).  
- Indore and Hyderabad are the best reported underwriting outcomes in **FY26**, but both are small scale and partly reserve-supported.   
o	Indore: **UWR** â‚ą6m to â‚ą15m (+â‚ą9m), **COR** 54% to -7% (-61 pts), driven by **IBNR** release improvement from +â‚ą6m to -â‚ą20m (-â‚ą26m).  
o	Hyderabad: **UWR** â‚ą(17)m to â‚ą4m (+â‚ą21m), **COR** **264**% to 67% (-**197** pts), driven by **NIC** dropping from â‚ą23m to â‚ą(8)m (-â‚ą31m).  
- Corporate is not the solution despite a positive **FY25**. Corporate **UWR** moved from â‚ą105m profit to â‚ą39m loss (-â‚ą144m), with **IBNR** swinging from a release of â‚ą85m to a charge of â‚ą57m (+â‚ą142m adverse) and **COR** worsening from -1,**752**% to **589**%. This cell is too small and too distorted by reserves to use as a strategic anchor.  
- There is almost no clean profitable growth at scale. If judged commercially, most â€śimprovementsâ€ť came from reserve release or low-claims one-offs, while the only meaningful growth geography, Mumbai, remained loss-making.  
- Management should focus immediately on three things:   
## Fix expense intensity (the biggest structural issue),  
## Diagnose reserve-dependence (IBNR support collapsed by â‚ą156m),  
## Stop rewarding gross volume when retained/earned profitability remains weak.

## Overall Portfolio Analysis  
Premium movement  
- **GWP** declined from â‚ą1,770m to â‚ą1,649m, an absolute decline of â‚ą121m (-6.8%).  
- Prop ceding reduced from â‚ą1,339m to â‚ą1,245m (-â‚ą94m, -7.0%).  
- Non-prop reduced from â‚ą88m to â‚ą76m (-â‚ą12m, -13.6%).  
- **NWP** declined from â‚ą343m to â‚ą328m (-â‚ą15m, -4.4%).  
Interpretation  
Top-line erosion is relatively limited. The gross book is not collapsing. In fact, retained premium fell less than **GWP**, which is mildly positive from a pure retention perspective.  
Business implication  
The portfolioâ€™s deterioration cannot be explained by gross premium shrinkage alone. The loss outcome is coming from claims/reserve movement and cost burden, not from a dramatic loss of business.  
________________________________________  
Retention / ceding movement  
- Retention ratio (**NWP**/**GWP**):   
o	**YTD**-Mar-25: 19.4%  
o	**YTD**-Mar-26: 19.9%  
o	Movement: +0.5 pts  
- Ceding ratio ((Prop + Non-prop)/**GWP**):   
o	**YTD**-Mar-25: 80.6%  
o	**YTD**-Mar-26: 80.1%  
o	Movement: -0.5 pts  
Interpretation  
This is one of the few positive underlying movements:  
- the portfolio remains heavily ceded,  
- but the degree of ceding is broadly stable to slightly improved.  
Business implication  
The deterioration is not due to the company retaining materially more risk in **FY26**. If anything, the reinsurance structure is broadly stable. This shifts the focus back to:  
- reserve support disappearing,  
- expense inflation,  
- and poor operating leverage.  
________________________________________  
**NEP** movement  
- **NEP** increased from â‚ą320m to â‚ą352m (+â‚ą32m, +10.0%)  
- PY **URR** increased from â‚ą199m to â‚ą222m (+â‚ą23m, +11.6%)  
- **URR** Charge reduced from â‚ą452m to â‚ą447m (-â‚ą5m, -1.1%)  
- CY Release increased from â‚ą230m to â‚ą249m (+â‚ą19m, +8.3%)  
- **NEP**/**GWP** improved from 18.1% to 21.4% (+3.3 pts)  
Interpretation  
This is important: despite lower **GWP** and slightly lower **NWP**, the portfolio actually generated more earned premium.  
Business implication  
If the book had merely maintained **FY25** claims and cost structure, the **NEP** increase should have supported profitability. The fact that profitability worsened sharply means the issue is elsewhere â€” primarily reserve dependence fading and expense burden rising.  
________________________________________  
Claims movement  
**NIC** Before **IBNR**  
- â‚ą240m to â‚ą211m  
- Absolute change: -â‚ą29m  
- Percentage change: -12.1%  
**IBNR**  
- â‚ą(**166**)m to â‚ą(10)m  
- Absolute change: +â‚ą156m adverse  
- In plain terms: prior year had a large reserve release, while current year had almost no reserve release left.  
**NIC** After **IBNR**  
- â‚ą74m to â‚ą202m  
- Absolute change: +â‚ą128m  
- Percentage change: +**173**.0%  
Ratios  
- Financial Loss Ratio: 23% to 57% (+34 pts)  
- Incurred LR: 75% to 60% (-15 pts)  
Interpretation of ratio contradiction  
There is a major contradiction:  
- **NIC** After **IBNR** increased sharply, yet  
- Incurred LR improved from 75% to 60%.  
This suggests the two ratio lines in the source are not aligned in the same way as the absolute incurred figures (possibly different denominator/definition logic in the dashboard extract).  
Possible interpretation based on available data: the ratio field is being computed on a basis not directly matching the displayed aggregate **NIC**/**NEP** totals.  
Business implication  
Decision-making should rely more on the absolute movement in **NIC** Before/After **IBNR** and **UWR**, not blindly on the extracted ratio fields where they conflict with the arithmetic.  
________________________________________  
**IBNR** / reserve effect  
- Prior year reserve effect: â‚ą166m release  
- Current year reserve effect: â‚ą10m release  
- Adverse swing: â‚ą156m  
Interpretation  
**FY25** underwriting result was materially supported by reserve release. **FY26** lost most of that support.  
Business implication  
This is the most important underwriting-quality insight:  
- **FY25** looked better than the â€ścleanâ€ť run-rate,  
- **FY26** deterioration is partly real, but partly also reflects that prior-year benefit did not repeat.  
________________________________________  
Expense ratio  
- Expense in absolute terms increased from â‚ą307m to â‚ą373m (+â‚ą66m, +21.5%)  
- Expense Ratio increased from 90% to **114**% (+24 pts)  
Interpretation  
This is the single largest structural profitability problem. A portfolio with **114**% expense ratio has no room for error.  
Business implication  
Even if claims normalize and reserve support returns partially, this book remains structurally weak unless the expense base is addressed.  
________________________________________  
Acquisition cost ratio  
- Acquisition cost stayed flat at â‚ą281m  
- Acquisition cost ratio worsened from 16% to 17% (+1 pt)  
Interpretation  
Acquisition cost did not rise, which is relatively positive, but it also did not reduce in line with pressure on underwriting margins.  
Business implication  
Acquisition spend is not the primary problem, but it is also not calibrated tightly enough to offset the high expense burden.  
________________________________________  
Commission ratio  
- RI Commission fell from â‚ą380m to â‚ą309m (-â‚ą71m, -18.7%)  
- Commission Ratio moved from -29% to -9% (+20 pts)  
Interpretation  
The portfolio received significantly less reinsurance commission support in **FY26**.  
Business implication  
This is another important negative lever:  
- lower RI commission reduced the offset against acquisition/expense burden,  
- which amplified the underwriting deterioration.  
________________________________________  
Underwriting result  
- UW Result: â‚ą37m â†’ â‚ą(**194**)m  
- Absolute deterioration: -â‚ą231m  
Drivers of deterioration  
## IBNR support weakened by â‚ą156m  
## Expense increased by â‚ą66m  
## RI commission fell by â‚ą71m  
## Claims before IBNR improved by â‚ą29m, but not enough to offset the above  
Overall portfolio quality  
The overall portfolio is worsening materially.  
The deterioration is driven less by gross premium or retention and more by:  
- disappearing reserve releases,  
- falling RI commission support,  
- and severe expense inflation.

## Underwriting Perspective  
Portfolio profitability quality  
The portfolioâ€™s reported underwriting quality is weak because:  
- expense ratio is already above **100**%,  
- net incurred claims increased materially,  
- and **FY25** earnings were flattered by reserve release.  
Clean underwriting view  
- Positive: **GWP** decline is modest, **NWP** stable, **NEP** up, **NIC** Before **IBNR** down  
- Negative: reserve support disappeared, cost base inflated, RI commission support fell  
Conclusion  
This is not a portfolio collapsing from bad sales alone. It is a portfolio whose earnings were previously held up by:  
- reserve releases,  
- RI commission support,  
- and insufficiently challenged cost structure.  
________________________________________  
Adequacy of premium versus claims  
Premium adequacy  
- **NEP** increased â‚ą32m (+10%)  
- **NIC** Before **IBNR** reduced â‚ą29m (-12%)  
- On those two metrics alone, premium adequacy actually looks slightly better.  
Butâ€¦  
- **IBNR** support collapsed by â‚ą156m  
- Expense increased by â‚ą66m  
- RI commission fell by â‚ą71m  
Implication  
The core problem is not traditional â€śpremium inadequate for current-year claimsâ€ť in every cell. It is:  
- thin retained economics  
- plus excessive dependence on reserve release  
- plus very high expense load  
________________________________________  
Reserve dependence  
This portfolio is clearly reserve-dependent.  
Why?  
- **IBNR** went from â‚ą(**166**)m to â‚ą(10)m  
- That alone worsened results by â‚ą156m  
Segments / locations with notable reserve-release dependence  
- Delhi: **IBNR** â‚ą(87)m to â‚ą5m (+â‚ą92m adverse) â†’ key reason **UWR** moved â‚ą58m to â‚ą(78)m  
- Bangalore: **IBNR** â‚ą(20)m to â‚ą22m (+â‚ą42m adverse) â†’ key reason **UWR** moved â‚ą6m to â‚ą(22)m  
- Kolkata: **IBNR** â‚ą(15)m to â‚ą7m (+â‚ą22m adverse)  
- Corporate: **IBNR** â‚ą(85)m to â‚ą57m (+â‚ą142m adverse)  
- Retail: still received reserve benefit, but less meaningful than prior year and not enough to offset expense  
Business implication  
Underwriting profit in this portfolio is not yet sustainable. **FY25** was boosted by reserve release; **FY26** shows what happens when that support fades.

Pricing / deductible / wording / referral / reinsurance implications  
Pricing

o	Delhi  
o	Kolkata  
o	Bangalore  
o	Retail  
o	Corporate  
Deductible / terms  
- Increase deductibles / tighten wordings where reserve support previously masked real loss cost.  
- For fire-style subsegments, review conditions and sum insured adequacy.  
Referral  
- Mandatory referral for:   
o	large Delhi / Kolkata accounts,  
o	distressed Retail cohorts,  
o	and any case with high acquisition cost but weak net margin.  
Reinsurance  
- Reinsurance structure itself is not the main deterioration driver this year because ceding is broadly stable.  
- Focus should be on ensuring the retained business is profitable after very high fixed expense allocation.

- Overall Product Deep Dive â€“ Bharat Sookshma  
- One-line summary: A heavily reinsured, expense-heavy portfolio that lost underwriting profitability in **FY26** despite better earned premium.  
- Top positive point: **NEP** increased from â‚ą320m to â‚ą352m (+â‚ą32m, +10.0%), and **NIC** Before **IBNR** reduced from â‚ą240m to â‚ą211m (-â‚ą29m, -12.1%).  
- Top concern: **IBNR** support weakened by â‚ą156m, expense rose â‚ą66m, RI commission fell â‚ą71m, and **UWR** deteriorated â‚ą231m.  
- Underwriting interpretation: **FY25** result was helped by reserve release; **FY26** exposes the underlying weak expense structure.  
- RM interpretation: The book should not be managed for top-line stability alone; retained/earned profitability must drive sales strategy.  
- Recommended action: Portfolio correction and cost reset  
________________________________________

- One-line summary: Medium-scale cell that moved from marginal profit to loss.

- Top concern: **NEP** fell â‚ą36m â†’ â‚ą29m (-â‚ą7m, -19.4%), expense ratio worsened 93% â†’ **106**% (+13 pts), and **UWR** moved â‚ą6m â†’ â‚ą(7)m (-â‚ą13m).

## Key Risks and Red Flags  
- Margin compression / outright loss: **UWR** â‚ą37m â†’ â‚ą(**194**)m  
- **COR** deterioration: 84% â†’ **162**% (+78 pts)  
- Reserve dependency: **IBNR** release shrank from â‚ą166m to â‚ą10m  
- Expense overload: Expense ratio 90% â†’ **114**%  
- Absolute expense inflation: â‚ą307m â†’ â‚ą373m (+â‚ą66m)  
- RI commission support weakened: â‚ą380m â†’ â‚ą309m (-â‚ą71m)  
- Retail value destruction despite better claims  
- Delhi and Kolkata adverse claims emergence  
- Bangalore reserve deterioration  
- Mumbai premium up but underwriting still loss-making  
- Acquisition inefficiency in **SME** Broking / Pune / Indore  
- No large, clean profitable growth engine  
- Very high ceding and very thin retained economics  
- Some segment/location ratios are distorted by prior-year reserve release, so management could overestimate performance if not normalized

ď‚§	current-year loss experience

## Final Conclusion  
The Bharat Sookshma portfolio is deteriorating.  
- Is the portfolio improving or deteriorating?  
Deteriorating materially.  
The book moved from â‚ą37m profit to â‚ą194m loss, with **COR** worsening by 78 pts.  
- Is growth profitable or poor quality?  
Mostly poor quality. There is almost no clean, large-scale profitable growth. Where premium is growing or being defended, it is often not translating to underwriting profit.  
- Which areas should be scaled?  
No large-scale area should be scaled aggressively today.  
Only selective growth is justified in:  
o	Emerging  
o	Indore  
o	Network partner  
o	Selected Hyderabad cohorts  
- Which areas should be corrected?  
o	Retail  
o	Delhi  
o	Kolkata  
o	Bangalore  
o	Mumbai cost structure  
- Which areas should be de-risked?  
o	Corporate  
o	**SME** Broking  
o	any stressed low-margin cohort with high acquisition and expense burden  
Sharp final view  
This is not primarily a premium problem. It is a portfolio quality and cost problem:  
- reserve support has faded,  
- expense is structurally too high,  
- RI commission support is lower,  
- and too much of the portfolio sits in poor-quality Retail economics.  
Management should immediately shift from top-line management to margin governance.

## Key portfolio message  
- Bharat Sookshma moved from marginal underwriting profit to material underwriting loss.   
o	UW Result: â‚ą37m profit â†’ â‚ą194m loss (-â‚ą231m)  
o	**COR**: 84% â†’ **162**% (+78 pts)  
- This is not a topline collapse story.   
o	**GWP**: â‚ą1,770m â†’ â‚ą1,649m (-â‚ą121m, -6.8%)  
o	**NWP**: â‚ą343m â†’ â‚ą328m (-â‚ą15m, -4.4%)  
o	**NEP**: â‚ą320m â†’ â‚ą352m (+â‚ą32m, +10.0%)  
- The portfolio deteriorated despite higher earned premium because reserve support faded and expenses rose sharply.   
o	**NIC** Before **IBNR**: â‚ą240m â†’ â‚ą211m (-â‚ą29m, -12.1%)  
o	**IBNR**: â‚ą(**166**)m â†’ â‚ą(10)m (+â‚ą156m adverse swing)  
o	**NIC** After **IBNR**: â‚ą74m â†’ â‚ą202m (+â‚ą128m, +**173**.0%)  
o	Expense: â‚ą307m â†’ â‚ą373m (+â‚ą66m, +21.5%)  
- Structural issue: the book is too expense-heavy for the retained premium base.   
o	Expense Ratio: 90% â†’ **114**% (+24 pts)  
o	Acq Cost %: 16% â†’ 17% (+1 pt)  
- Bottom line: this is a margin and portfolio-quality problem, not just a premium problem.  
________________________________________  
## Underwriting message  
- Underwriting quality worsened materially.   
o	UW Result: â‚ą37m â†’ â‚ą(**194**)m  
o	**COR**: 84% â†’ **162**%  
- Claims before reserve were better, but final incurred outcome worsened because prior reserve release did not repeat.   
o	**NIC** Before **IBNR**: -â‚ą29m improvement  
o	**IBNR** support weakened by â‚ą156m  
- Reserve dependence is high. **FY25** profitability was materially flattered by reserve release; **FY26** exposed the cleaner run-rate.  
- Retail is the largest underwriting drag by scale.   
o	Retail **UWR**: â‚ą(91)m â†’ â‚ą(**162**)m (-â‚ą71m)  
o	Retail **COR**: **126**% â†’ **157**% (+31 pts)  
o	Even though Retail **NIC** improved from â‚ą174m to â‚ą143m (-â‚ą31m), expense increased from â‚ą272m to â‚ą346m (+â‚ą74m).  
- Largest zone-level deterioration came from Delhi and Kolkata.   
o	Delhi **UWR**: â‚ą58m â†’ â‚ą(78)m (-â‚ą136m)  
o	Kolkata **UWR**: â‚ą13m â†’ â‚ą(46)m (-â‚ą59m)  
- Best reported underwriting outcomes are in smaller pockets, but many are reserve-assisted rather than structurally strong.   
o	Indore: **UWR** â‚ą6m â†’ â‚ą15m, **COR** 54% â†’ -7%  
o	Hyderabad: **UWR** â‚ą(17)m â†’ â‚ą4m, **COR** **264**% â†’ 67%  
Leadership takeaway:  
The book needs underwriting repair by segment and geography, not just portfolio-level premium defense.  
________________________________________  
## RM message  
- Sales quality is weak in the largest parts of the book.  
- Most defended or growing premium is not translating into underwriting value.   
o	Mumbai:   
ď‚§	**GWP**: â‚ą540m â†’ â‚ą595m (+â‚ą55m, +10.2%)  
ď‚§	**NEP**: â‚ą85m â†’ â‚ą110m (+â‚ą25m, +29.4%)  
ď‚§	**UWR**: â‚ą(14)m â†’ â‚ą(28)m (-â‚ą14m)  
ď‚§	Implication: growth is coming through, but it is poor-quality growth because expense inflation consumed the claims benefit.  
- Delhi is a clear example where better earned premium did not convert into profitability.   
o	**NEP**: â‚ą81m â†’ â‚ą89m (+â‚ą8m, +9.9%)  
o	**UWR**: â‚ą58m â†’ â‚ą(78)m (-â‚ą136m)  
- RMs should stop prioritising topline stability in Retail clusters unless cost and profitability are proven.  
- Better RM focus should move to smaller, more controllable pockets:   
o	Emerging  
o	Indore  
o	selective Hyderabad  
o	Network partner  
- Mumbai should not be presented as success purely on premium growth.  
- Acquisition efficiency needs tighter control.   
o	**SME** Broking Acq %: 9% â†’ 37%  
o	Pune Acq %: 18% â†’ 25%  
o	Indore Acq %: 16% â†’ 27%  
Leadership takeaway:  
RM strategy should shift from **GWP**-led management to retained-profit-led management.

## Top 5 concerns: Zone and Vertical wise  
1. Retail (Vertical) â€“ biggest structural concern  
- **UWR**: â‚ą(91)m â†’ â‚ą(**162**)m (-â‚ą71m)  
- **COR**: **126**% â†’ **157**% (+31 pts)  
- Expense: â‚ą272m â†’ â‚ą346m (+â‚ą74m, +27.2%)  
- Message: claims improved, but the segment still destroyed value because the cost structure is too heavy.  
2. Delhi (Zone) â€“ biggest deterioration at scale  
- **UWR**: â‚ą58m â†’ â‚ą(78)m (-â‚ą136m)  
- **NIC**: â‚ą(34)m â†’ â‚ą85m (+â‚ą119m)  
- **COR**: 27% â†’ **194**% (+**167** pts)  
- Message: scale remained high, but underwriting quality collapsed.  
3. Kolkata (Zone) â€“ severe claims/reserve deterioration  
- **UWR**: â‚ą13m â†’ â‚ą(46)m (-â‚ą59m)  
- **NIC**: â‚ą(2)m â†’ â‚ą45m (+â‚ą47m)  
- **COR**: 50% â†’ **266**% (+**216** pts)  
- Message: clear underwriting stress; should not be treated as defend-at-all-costs business.  
4. Mumbai (Zone) â€“ premium growth but still poor-quality economics  
- **GWP**: â‚ą540m â†’ â‚ą595m (+â‚ą55m)  
- **NEP**: â‚ą85m â†’ â‚ą110m (+â‚ą25m)  
- **UWR**: â‚ą(14)m â†’ â‚ą(28)m (-â‚ą14m)  
- Expense: â‚ą98m â†’ â‚ą134m (+â‚ą36m)  
- Message: growth came through, but profitability worsened. This is a leadership red flag.  
5. **SME** Broking (Vertical) â€“ cost efficiency has broken down  
- **UWR**: â‚ą2m â†’ â‚ą(2)m  
- Acq Cost %: 9% â†’ 37%  
- Expense Ratio: **206**% â†’ **289**%  
- Message: too small and too expensive; current economics do not justify growth effort.  
________________________________________  
## Immediate actions  
## Reset Retail profitability  
- Re-underwrite Retail cohorts immediately.  
- Focus on expense leakage, not just pricing.  
- No volume-led push unless minimum profitability thresholds are met.  
## Deep-dive Delhi and Kolkata  
- Split deterioration into:   
o	current-year claims emergence  
o	prior-year reserve normalization  
o	account mix / pricing issue  
- Freeze aggressive growth until those books are repaired.  
## Stop rewarding unprofitable growth  
- Mumbai should not be seen as a â€śgood growthâ€ť market unless **UWR** improves.  
- RM scorecards should move from **GWP** to **NEP** / **COR** / **UWR** discipline.  
## Tighten acquisition economics  
- Review payout / acquisition model in:   
o	**SME** Broking  
o	Pune  
o	Indore  
o	low-margin Retail cohorts  
## Protect and selectively grow better-quality pockets  
- Emerging  
- Indore  
- Hyderabad  
- Network Partner  
- only renewal-led, technically profitable slices  
## Build reserve-adjusted view of profitability  
- **FY25** was materially helped by reserve release.  
- Leadership needs monthly visibility on:   
o	current accident-year loss ratio  
o	prior-year development  
o	pure expense burden  
________________________________________

- Retail **UWR** and **COR**  
- Delhi / Kolkata / Mumbai watchlist metrics

## Key portfolio message  
- **ICICI** Bharat Laghu Udyam Suraksha has moved from underwriting profit to underwriting loss.   
o	UW Result: â‚ą161m profit â†’ â‚ą99m loss (-â‚ą260m deterioration)  
o	**COR**: -7% â†’ **161**% (+**168** pts)  
- This is not a premium-retention problem; it is a reserve-normalisation + expense deterioration story.   
o	**GWP**: â‚ą1,017m â†’ â‚ą932m (-â‚ą85m, -8.4%)  
o	**NWP**: â‚ą158m â†’ â‚ą164m (+â‚ą6m, +3.8%)  
o	**NEP**: â‚ą150m â†’ â‚ą158m (+â‚ą8m, +5.3%)  
- Underlying claims before **IBNR** improved sharply, but prior-year reserve benefit reversed.   
o	**NIC** Before **IBNR**: â‚ą196m â†’ â‚ą112m (-â‚ą84m, -42.9%)  
o	**IBNR**: â‚ą(**211**)m â†’ â‚ą83m (+â‚ą294m adverse swing)  
o	**NIC** After **IBNR**: â‚ą(16)m â†’ â‚ą195m (+â‚ą211m deterioration)  
- Expense inflation further weakened the book.   
o	Expense: â‚ą120m â†’ â‚ą149m (+â‚ą29m, +24.2%)  
o	Expense Ratio: 76% â†’ 91% (+15 pts)  
- Retention actually improved.   
o	Retention (**NWP**/**GWP**): 15.5% â†’ 17.6% (+2.1 pts)  
o	Ceding ratio: 84.4% â†’ 82.4% (-2.0 pts)  
- Leadership takeaway: **FY25** profitability was materially supported by reserve release; **FY26** reveals the cleaner underlying earnings profile.  
________________________________________  
## Underwriting message  
- The headline underwriting deterioration is primarily reserve-driven, not gross claims-driven.   
o	Current-year reported claims improved, but reserve support disappeared.  
- Large deterioration pockets are Delhi and Kolkata.   
o	Delhi:   
ď‚§	**NEP**: â‚ą41m â†’ â‚ą43m (+â‚ą2m, +4.9%)  
ď‚§	**NIC** After **IBNR**: â‚ą(15)m â†’ â‚ą98m (+â‚ą113m)  
ď‚§	UW Result: â‚ą57m â†’ â‚ą(72)m (-â‚ą129m)  
ď‚§	**COR**: -36% â†’ **273**% (+**309** pts)  
o	Kolkata:   
ď‚§	**NEP**: â‚ą14m â†’ â‚ą17m (+â‚ą3m, +21.4%)  
ď‚§	**NIC** After **IBNR**: â‚ą(56)m â†’ â‚ą75m (+â‚ą131m)  
ď‚§	UW Result: â‚ą70m â†’ â‚ą(71)m (-â‚ą141m)  
ď‚§	**COR**: -**409**% â†’ **531**% (+**940** pts)  
- Retail has turned from profitable to loss-making at meaningful scale.   
o	Retail **UWR**: â‚ą52m â†’ â‚ą(17)m (-â‚ą69m)  
o	Retail **COR**: 46% â†’ **111**% (+65 pts)  
o	Retail Expense Ratio: 78% â†’ **100**% (+22 pts)  
- Corporate remains the strongest vertical technically.   
o	**UWR**: â‚ą34m â†’ â‚ą38m (+â‚ą4m)  
o	**COR**: -6% â†’ -26% (-20 pts)  
o	**NIC**: â‚ą21m â†’ â‚ą6m (-â‚ą15m, -71.4%)  
- Best zone-level underwriting improvement came from Pune and Chennai.   
o	Pune: **UWR** â‚ą(42)m â†’ â‚ą29m (+â‚ą71m), **NIC** â‚ą49m â†’ â‚ą(24)m (-â‚ą73m), **COR** **426**% â†’ -**113**%  
o	Chennai: **UWR** â‚ą(3)m â†’ â‚ą16m (+â‚ą19m), **NIC** â‚ą9m â†’ â‚ą(10)m (-â‚ą19m), **COR** **139**% â†’ -81%  
- Leadership takeaway:  
The book needs reserve-adjusted underwriting review by zone, especially Delhi, Kolkata, and Retail.  
________________________________________  
## RM message  
- RM quality is mixed; there is very little clean profitable growth at scale.  
- Mumbai is the only major zone showing gross and retained growth, but it is still not value-accretive enough.   
o	**GWP**: â‚ą421m â†’ â‚ą463m (+â‚ą42m, +10.0%)  
o	**NWP**: â‚ą60m â†’ â‚ą71m (+â‚ą11m, +18.3%)  
o	**NEP**: â‚ą49m â†’ â‚ą52m (+â‚ą3m, +6.1%)  
o	**UWR**: â‚ą18m â†’ â‚ą0m (-â‚ą18m)  
o	Message: premium growth came through, but profit disappeared.  
- Delhi is a classic case of defending business without underwriting quality.   
o	**GWP**: â‚ą233m â†’ â‚ą193m (-â‚ą40m, -17.2%)  
o	**NWP**: â‚ą38m â†’ â‚ą39m (+â‚ą1m)  
o	**NEP**: â‚ą41m â†’ â‚ą43m (+â‚ą2m)  
o	**UWR**: â‚ą57m â†’ â‚ą(72)m  
o	Message: RM defence did not protect margin.  
- Kolkata is not a market where more premium should be chased.   
o	**GWP**: â‚ą84m â†’ â‚ą75m (-10.7%)  
o	**NEP**: â‚ą14m â†’ â‚ą17m (+21.4%)  
o	**UWR**: â‚ą70m â†’ â‚ą(71)m  
- Better commercial focus should be on segments with cleaner economics.   
o	Corporate  
o	Emerging  
o	selective Chennai / Pune  
- Acquisition effectiveness is weakening in some small books.   
o	**SME** Broking Acq %: 17% â†’ 21%  
o	Emerging Acq %: 14% â†’ 18%  
o	Kolkata Acq %: 11% â†’ 15%  
- Leadership takeaway:  
RM strategy should shift from **GWP** defence to **NEP** + **UWR** quality gates.

## Top 5 concerns: Zone and Vertical wise  
1. Kolkata (Zone)  
- **UWR**: â‚ą70m â†’ â‚ą(71)m (-â‚ą141m)  
- **NIC**: â‚ą(56)m â†’ â‚ą75m (+â‚ą131m)  
- **COR**: -**409**% â†’ **531**%  
- Message: largest absolute deterioration outside Delhi; clear red zone.  
2. Delhi (Zone)  
- **UWR**: â‚ą57m â†’ â‚ą(72)m (-â‚ą129m)  
- **NIC**: â‚ą(15)m â†’ â‚ą98m (+â‚ą113m)  
- **COR**: -36% â†’ **273**%  
- Message: scale remains large, but underwriting has broken down.  
3. Retail (Vertical)  
- **UWR**: â‚ą52m â†’ â‚ą(17)m (-â‚ą69m)  
- **COR**: 46% â†’ **111**%  
- Expense: â‚ą84m â†’ â‚ą119m (+â‚ą35m, +41.7%)  
- Message: largest scale segment is now value-destructive.  
4. **SME** Broking (Vertical)  
- **UWR**: â‚ą(97)m â†’ â‚ą(14)m (improved but still loss-making)  
- **COR**: 1,**894**% â†’ **342**%  
- Acq Cost %: 17% â†’ 21%  
- Message: still structurally weak despite better claims.  
5. Mumbai (Zone)  
- **GWP** up, but profit disappeared  
- **UWR**: â‚ą18m â†’ â‚ą0m  
- **COR**: 64% â†’ 96%  
- Expense: â‚ą51m â†’ â‚ą67m (+â‚ą16m)  
- Message: growth without profit conversion.  
________________________________________  
## Immediate actions  
## Deep-dive Delhi and Kolkata immediately  
- Separate:   
o	current-year claims  
o	prior-year reserve impact  
o	account mix deterioration  
- These two zones drove the largest underwriting collapse.  
## Protect and selectively scale Corporate  
- It is the only meaningful vertical with positive, sustained underwriting profitability.  
- Use Corporate underwriting discipline as benchmark for other segments.  
## Reset Retail profitability  
- No growth push until Retail meets clear gate metrics on:   
o	**COR**  
o	Expense ratio  
o	**UWR** per **NEP**  
- Current Retail economics are not acceptable.  
## Reframe Mumbai  
- Treat Mumbai as a scale market under watch, not a success story.  
- Require profitability guardrails before further expansion.  
## Keep Pune and Chennai as selective growth / repair pilots  
- Best visible zone improvements  
- Scale only after confirming sustainability beyond reserve effects  
## Tighten SME Broking and weak small-zone economics  
- Revisit acquisition payout and underwriting thresholds  
- Do not carry structurally poor small-book economics  
________________________________________
